Taiwanese Tobacco Smugglers in Fuzhou Open Fire and Wound Our Police—Arrested Ronin Reclaimed by Japanese Consulate

Fuzhou Dispatch: Fujian Province is separated from Taiwan by only a narrow strip of water, a mere two-day journey. Consequently, unemployed vagrants from Taiwan flock to Fujian to make a living, with the largest numbers concentrated in the coastal areas of Xiamen, Fuzhou, and Quanzhou. It is estimated that there are already over a thousand Taiwanese in Fuzhou alone, all engaged in running opium dens and "tu-xing" (local products) businesses. According to investigations by the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, within the police district alone, there are over three hundred Japanese-run foreign-brand liquor stores and over forty "tu-xing" businesses. Moreover, the Taiwanese Association has selected over two hundred strong and fierce ruffians and formed a "Taiwanese Overseas Chinese Volunteer Corps," issued with handguns by the consulate, to be solely responsible for protection. When our government officials wish to search these establishments, they must notify the consulate and dispatch Japanese police to accompany them. Otherwise, they will open fire to resist arrest. Even if criminals are apprehended, they must be handed over to the Japanese police for interrogation and trial. Our government officials are not allowed to intervene. These foreign-brand opium dens have become places that harbor dirt and accept filth. All thieves gather within.

Page 8

They are planning and conspiring, thus not only undermining the opium ban but also disrupting public order. Our government officials have no power to intervene, so nothing can be done. The Taiwanese have become increasingly reckless. On the evening of October 7th, the detective team of the Public Security Bureau received a tip that someone was smuggling a large quantity of opium to Liangtai Dexing Lane. They dispatched several detectives to investigate and arrested one unidentified person with three large packages of opium. As they were about to take him back to the station, suddenly more than thirty Taiwanese thugs, each armed with handguns, iron bars, and knives, surrounded the detectives, intending to seize both the person and the goods. The detectives resisted but were overpowered and everything was taken away. Fortunately, the inspection team of the Public Security Bureau stationed nearby on Tiantang Street heard the news and rushed to rescue them, arriving at Dexing Lane. They joined the detectives in a vigorous pursuit. Unexpectedly, the thugs, seeing people chasing from behind, opened fire. The inspection team also returned fire. For a moment, stray bullets flew everywhere, causing great panic among the merchants and residents, who all closed their doors. The chaos lasted for about half an hour before the thugs were repelled. Six perpetrators were arrested on the spot. However, four of our inspectors and detectives were also wounded. The inspection team escorted the criminals to the Public Security Bureau. One of them, Li Caiwang, was an employee of the Japanese Consulate. On the 8th, the Japanese Consul sent a letter requesting extradition. The Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, considering that the Taiwanese had not only smuggled opium but also opened fire and wounded our police, which was extremely illegal, only handed over Li Caiwang for repatriation. At 10:00 AM on the 9th, the Japanese Consul Moriya, accompanied by Police Chief Zhongshan and Ke Baoluo, representatives of the Taiwanese Association, visited Qiu Zhaochen, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, requesting that the other five people also be handed over to them for repatriation. Negotiations lasted until 2:00 PM. The Japanese Consul agreed to the conditions proposed by our side: (1) compensation for all losses of the wounded police; (2) severe punishment of the ronin who opened fire and robbed; (3) prohibition of the "Volunteer Corps" organization which disrupts public order. Therefore, the five Taiwanese were handed over to them for interrogation and trial. (October 11th)

Guangdong and Guizhou Assist Each Other to Expand Strength: Wang Jialie Purchases Weapons from Guangdong; Chen Jitang Recruits Soldiers from Guizhou; War in Guizhou is Imminent

Guangzhou Dispatch: Messengers from the provinces of Guangxi, Guizhou, and Guangdong are constantly traveling back and forth. Chen Jitang of Guangdong Province previously dispatched Mai Huanzhang, Gan Jiayi, and Dan Lianxin to Guizhou to negotiate important matters on behalf of the Southwest Political Council. It is now learned that Mai and others returned to Guangdong via Guizhou on the 1st of this month, passing through Guangxi Province eastward. They are expected to arrive in Guangzhou around the middle of this month.

Guizhou Province is located in a remote western area, with inconvenient transportation. There is a great shortage of military supplies. Wang Jialie, the Chairman of the province, recently purchased a large batch of guns and artillery from Guangdong, including dozens of rapid-firing guns and hundreds of thousands of rounds of ammunition. These have already been transported from Guangdong, transiting through Guangxi to Guizhou. Recently, Wang felt that the purchased artillery and guns were still insufficient. Yesterday, he telegraphed Chen Jitang again, requesting the purchase of 200 Type 79 light machine guns and 50,000 rounds of ammunition from Guangdong. This has been agreed to here and will be shipped to Guiyang shortly. Wang has entrusted Guangdong with purchasing military supplies. Chen Jitang, recently needing new soldiers to replenish his armies, finds recruitment within Guangdong difficult. Therefore, he has entrusted Wang Jialie with recruiting two regiments of new soldiers (approximately 3,000 men) in Guizhou. It is now learned that these new soldiers have already been recruited and have been dispatched from Guiyang through Guangxi, passing through Hechi, and arriving in Liuzhou. They will travel to Wuzhou along the Guiping Road and then take civilian boats to Guangdong. They are expected to arrive around the middle of this month. Chen Jitang, upon receiving the news, dispatched Tang, the captain of the 12th Gendarmerie Team, with the entire team of gendarmes to Wuzhou on the 5th of this month to prepare to receive the new soldiers arriving in the province. In addition to recruiting several thousand soldiers for Chen Jitang, Wang has also selected 24 fine horses in Guizhou and sent several adjutants to escort them to Guangdong for Chen Jitang to receive. Chen completed the inspection and receipt on the 4th.

Internal wars in Guizhou are frequent. According to military news, the Guizhou army units of Jiang Zaizhen and Che Mingyi have returned to Guizhou from the Sichuan border. You Guocai's unit has also returned to Guizhou from Yunnan and set up a command post in Panjiang. You and others have jointly issued a telegram denouncing Wang Jialie. War in Guizhou is once again on the verge of breaking out. However, Wang Jialie's side sent a telegram to Guangdong on the 1st of this month, claiming to maintain peace. Wang's telegram stated, "Guizhou Province has suffered repeated military conflicts, leading to poverty and exhaustion of the people, coupled with drought, creating a desolate scene. Since returning to the province, I, Jialie, have felt remorse and, in addition to self-reproach, have spared no effort to compromise and concede to achieve peace, aiming to embody the national spirit of unity and save the country, desiring our people to breathe and recover. Therefore, I have fully accepted consultations with neighboring provinces. Messengers travel constantly. I have used every means possible to accommodate and conciliate You Guocai, repeatedly ceding the eight counties of Panjiang and requesting Peng Gongwu, Tan Xun, and Tao, among others, to wait for negotiations in Yunnan. I have also welcomed the Yunnan representative Dan Nugang and You's representative Liao Yinxiang to the province, discussing in detail several times, deciding to entrust the position of overall clearing and suppressing commander of the province. All this has factual proof and is known to people inside and outside the province. Unexpectedly, You recently sent telegrams to his representatives Deng Mingjie and Dong Jiangzhen, stating, on one hand, that 'previously, the troops crossed the river, originally intending to advance on three routes and restore the original defense. Unfortunately, Jiang and Che suffered defeats, so we stopped at the brink of disaster with the mediation of Yunnan Chairman Long Yun.' On the other hand, he stated that 'Liao Yinxiang's visit to the province was not entrusted with a task, but merely to engage in some dealings to ease the situation.' Finally, he fabricated facts and made false accusations, which have been published in various newspapers, causing people inside and outside the province to sigh and feel alarmed. I reflect again that due to my lack of virtue, sincerity has not been established, and persuasion has been ineffective. However, the will for peace will never change because of this. I vow to persevere in pacifying matters and ensuring tranquility. In addition to telegraphing Chairman Long to continue to take responsibility for mediation and retaining Dan and Liao, among others, for long-term consultations in order to avoid internal strife, I am especially telegraphing this to you for your attention." Considering Wang Jialie's telegram, while Wang Jialie is indeed talking about vigorously maintaining peace, he is also actively purchasing guns and artillery. Meanwhile, You Guocai and others have repeatedly telegraphed, denouncing Wang's misgovernment and claiming to petition for the people. With both sides going to extremes, it is feared that war in Guizhou cannot be eliminated by words and writings alone. (October 8th)

Chiang Promulgates Guidelines for Civil Disputes in Bandit Areas—Special Emphasis on Protecting Farmers' Interests—

Nanchang Dispatch: In the suppression of the Red Army in five provinces, the 19th Route Army of the Eastern Route has driven the Zhu-Mao pseudo-First Front Army out of JiangLe and Shaowu. The 1st, 3rd, 5th, and 7th Army Corps in Jiangxi are continuously attacking Lichuan, Nancheng, and Nanfeng. They are being intercepted by this Route Army. Fierce battles are breaking out east of Lichuan, Xiaoshi, and Xinfeng Street, close to the Fujian border. The National Army units of Zhou Wei, Zhou Hunyuan, Yao Chun, Wu Qiwai, and Xu Kexiang are exceptionally brave and have been fighting bloody battles with the bandits for four days, killing many bandits. Nancheng is still in the midst of a fierce battle. Recently, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, considering that the bandit areas will soon be recovered, has promulgated five articles of the "Guidelines for Handling Civil Disputes in Recovered Bandit Areas" in the five provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei to adapt to the special circumstances. Among them, special emphasis is placed on not blaming the past and protecting the interests of farmers to stabilize society. The articles are as follows:

(1) In handling civil disputes in various counties within the bandit suppression area, in addition to complying as much as possible with the current civil law, these guidelines may be applied. (2) When applying these guidelines, the principles of the current civil law should still be adopted as much as possible. However, if the situation has changed after the bandit rebellion, appropriate relief methods should be taken between the severity and urgency of the situation to achieve appropriate treatment. (3) These guidelines emphasize the protection of farmers' interests. The following methods will be used for all actions by farmers under duress from bandits:

(A) Regarding land and other real estate, disputes over boundaries or ownership arising after the bandit rebellion shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of Chapters One and Three of the "Regulations on the Handling of Rural Land in the Bandit Suppression Areas" in the provinces and Article 12 of the "Regulations on Military Colonization." (B) Regarding rental disputes over farmland resumed after the bandit rebellion, the handling procedures and methods shall comply with the provisions of Chapter Five of the "Regulations on the Handling of Rural Land." (C) Regarding farmer debt disputes after the bandit rebellion, the handling procedures and methods shall comply with the provisions of Chapter Seven of the "Regulations on Rural Land." The foregoing methods may also be applied to other displaced people in the bandit area who have newly returned. (4) All behaviors of the people other than those in the previous articles that violate the law were not originally intentional. If there are marriage matters, pledge matters, joint property matters, and all other personal matters and various problems that are driven by circumstances, resulting in a loss of normalcy, they should be handled with humanity and leniency as much as possible, within the possible scope of fact and law, and plans should be made for handling. (5) These guidelines shall not apply to bandit areas that have been recovered for more than one year and have not been changed, except that the Regulations on Rural Land Handling may still be consulted. (October 13th)

Verdict in the Wuchang Gold Digging Case: Peng Younan Found Guilty of Property Damage; Proceeds of the Theft Confiscated

Hankou Dispatch: The case of Peng Younan, a neighbor, stealing gold from Kong Geng's house in Wuchang on May 30th, was reported by Kong as property damage and theft. The Wuhan Garrison Headquarters ordered the entire committee of the Wuchang Construction Watchtower, together with the Wuchang Lawyers Association, to organize a Gold Digging Investigation Committee to be responsible for investigation and trial. This lasted three months. Because the volume of the gold cellar was quite large, the types of gold and the amount involved could not be accurately determined. Despite offering a reward, no one came forward with evidence. It was legally difficult to make a rash judgment. Under the supervision of the police department, the Investigation Committee convened the parties involved and witnesses on August 26th for a final public debate. It was determined that Peng Younan was indeed highly suspected of committing theft and property damage. Peng Shi-sun was also not without collusion in providing false evidence and conspiring to conceal stolen goods. It was resolved to send them to the Police Department's Military Law Office for detention. After the two Pengs were imprisoned, on the 14th of this month, the Police Department's Military Law Office formally announced the verdict. The principal offender, Peng Younan, damaged another person's property and was sentenced to one month of detention. The number of days of detention before the verdict was allowed to be offset by two days for each day of detention. Due to the crime of property damage, the proceeds of the theft, 24,500 yuan in silver dollars (the amount that Peng Younan was willing to pay as a fine), were confiscated and handed over to the Construction Committee of the Watchtower for use as construction funds. The theft portion could not be established because it did not meet the legal conditions. Peng Shi-sun was found not guilty. After the verdict, Peng Younan was returned to custody, and Peng Shi-sun was released. The case was thus concluded. The police authorities issued a statement on the same day, stating that [the Wuchang gold digging case, after the Investigation Committee reported the results of the investigation, along with their opinions, to the headquarters, the headquarters reviewed and verified the facts and could only make a judgment according to law. However, after the judgment, if anyone has new and reliable evidence regarding the quality, quantity, and detailed amount of gold that Peng has unearthed, they can still report to the headquarters in detail through the proper procedures of the previous announcement method, so that the headquarters can fully pursue and obtain it for the public good]. (October 14th)

Inspection Report on Jiangxi, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei by Our Special Correspondent Ren An: Miscellaneous News from Lianhua After the Robbery (Part Two)

Due to the National Army's adoption of a scorched-earth policy, advancing and firmly defending each captured location, the bandit forces in Lianhua County, facing a lack of military supplies and economic exhaustion, have been forced to retreat to dangerous locations in hopes of surviving. The pseudo-17th and 18th Divisions, recently gathered at the Meihuashan mountain ridge on the border of Chaling, attempted to lure the main force of the National Army away in mid-September, staging their so-called counter-offensive, hiding their main force in the deep mountains and dense forests of the Wangfo'an Xiaotian area. First, they sent a portion of the bandits to besiege the National Army's Xianling position, launching several fierce assaults. The National Army calmly responded and did not pursue. Several planes also conducted reconnaissance and bombing, but the bandits were unsuccessful and retreated under cover of night. Small-scale skirmishes between the pseudo-Red Guards, guerrillas, and anti-communist volunteer corps or the National Army's clearing and suppression teams are common within twenty miles of the city. Nancun, fifteen miles west of the city, was only recovered a few days ago. The reporter rushed to visit the village and saw two bloody wounded soldiers being carried back from the front lines. Soon after, a battalion commander named Guo also led his troops and said, "We fought with the bandits on the hillside about three miles from here. We knew that the bandits had about a hundred rifles, so we only led two platoons to clear and suppress the area. Unexpectedly, a new bandit force of over a hundred men and rifles had been transferred from Pingxiang, resulting in a great disparity in numbers. If we had not retreated quickly, we would have suffered a great loss." In addition to the aforementioned pseudo-17th and 18th Divisions, each with four or five thousand men and rifles, the current bandit forces in Lianhua also include various miscellaneous organizations such as the Red Guard, Political Security Team, and District Guerrilla, totaling about two hundred rifles. Their movements are unpredictable. Encounters like the one experienced by Battalion Commander Guo occur several times a day throughout the county, but they are all small-scale skirmishes with no major victories or defeats.

The trip to Nancun can also be considered an inspection of the front lines. The village is located in the mountains with a clear stream that can irrigate good farmland. The late rice is already laden with ears, growing lushly and deeply, so high that people can be lost in it. This shows that the fields in the bandit area are not as barren as those in the red-white transition zone. The stationed troops are rushing to build bunkers on the hilltop, and the villagers are helping them. At dusk, they all close their doors and live in seclusion. They are also unwilling to come out when they hear the alarm because they still harbor a wait-and-see attitude. Therefore, it is not convenient to carry out a thorough household registration and Baojia system. It is also difficult for the district office and volunteer corps personnel to patrol outdoors at night because the pseudo-county Soviet government is located in Miaoxia Village, only five miles away. To prevent bandit night attacks, they can only close their doors and guard themselves. The volunteer corps sells salt and kerosene to users for a fixed price. Each person is allowed to purchase three coins' worth of salt per day. A cloth-made license with a seal is required for purchasing. On the day in question, the volunteer corps had not gone to the city to purchase salt, so there was no salt to sell. Those who came to purchase were disappointed and returned, saying that the suffering of not having salt to eat was greater than not having oil to light lamps. The bandits divided the fields in the village twice. The first time, the area of the fields was used as a standard, with each person receiving about two dou (about two or three mu). The second time, the yield was used as a standard: four shi for high-quality fields, three shi for medium-quality fields, and two shi for low-quality fields, with each person receiving fields that could harvest seven shi of grain. Each shi weighs one hundred jin. A progressive tax of 6% should be paid, totaling 42 jin of grain. (Those who originally had eight shi of grain should pay a progressive tax of 7%, and so on. However, no one is allowed to receive more than fifteen shi, and in reality, no one has ever been heard of receiving more than ten shi). Each shi is priced at 4,000 wen based on the current market price. Hired farmers and poor farmers can pay the tax entirely in grain, while middle farmers can pay half in grain and half in cash, or choose as they please. Rich farmers must pay entirely in cash, and sometimes the price is raised to 6,000 wen per shi.

The items most affected by the blockade in the bandit area are salt and cloth. Even at high prices, they are not easily obtained. Last year, the bandits also implemented a blockade policy, prohibiting the export of rice, tea oil, metals, coal, wood, and other items. Later, seeing that glutinous rice could be used to brew wine and fetch a good price in non-bandit areas, they lifted the ban. Subsequently, tea oil, coal, and other items were also gradually allowed to be exported. When purchasing industrial products and daily necessities from outside, the cooperatives often handled it, exchanging the agricultural products of the bandit area for them. They rarely used cash unless absolutely necessary.

The bandits have occupied Lianhua County for many years, only paving a stone road in the city and building a dam in a certain area to develop water conservancy. An investigation after the city's recovery found that the bandits had established thirteen Lenin Elementary Schools. The word "Lenin" in the name of the Lenin Elementary Schools has been completely removed. It is said that formal elementary schools will be gradually established or children's anti-communist groups will be reorganized to implement special education. The stone road will be retained to facilitate transportation. The dam built in a certain village upstream, according to the refugees (mostly landlords and wealthy gentry) who had fled and returned home, harmed the feng shui, and they repeatedly petitioned the county government to demolish it. Their request was not approved, probably because they feared that countless fertile fields upstream would be turned into truly red land.

The people who have been banditized seem to have three characteristics. The first is fearlessness. During the previous National Army's suppression campaigns, they would flee dozens of miles away whenever the army arrived in an area, and few dared to risk returning. Now, they only flee slightly outside the village, and upon learning that the National Army is tolerant, they immediately return together. Some even dare to cross the heavy encirclement to seek revenge and take the heads of newly returned refugees. Villagers in Wutang were killed by the dozen for cutting electric wires as a warning, but they were still unafraid. They even took advantage of the retreat of a certain company to confiscate their guns with farm tools, resulting in a bloody massacre. Previously, they experienced a rice shortage and sent villagers to the bandit area to purchase grain, successfully attracting friends and relatives and helping to build bunkers in the rain of bullets, all without fear. Their courage is evident in this way. The second is cruelty. Killing is not considered a big deal, and there are countless examples. The third is creativity. Regarding positions such as the captain of the volunteer corps and other important positions in groups, the farmers dared to compete with the refugees. After winning the positions, they were often able to be innovative in their duties and handle them with ease. If they failed to compete, they would turn into troublemakers, making things difficult for those in charge.

The bandit army paid close attention to the training of the people, especially the organization and training of children, which was very rigorous and serious. The eleven-character slogan of the children's group was [Prepare, prepare at all times]. A careful examination of it can reveal its profound meaning. The reporter once spoke with children who had joined the children's group. First, their answers were very fluent, especially regarding the significance of memorial days such as May 1st, May 9th, September 18th, and January 28th, they answered fluently without hesitation. When using terms such as "dividing calendars for several years," "imperialism," and "bourgeoisie," they were even more familiar with them. The textbooks used in Lenin Elementary Schools only had three subjects in the lower grades: national language, singing, and physical education. The upper grades are unknown. There was no fixed time limit, and they were promoted or demoted according to their grades. The Commissioner's Office has organized the children in the city who have been educated by the bandits into anti-communist children's groups and provided them with special education. They have also been assigned to check and fill out forms for residents' household registration and occupation, among other things. Because they speak clearly, work hard, and achieve results above adults,

Statistics show that there are 265 shops in Liancheng, with the fewest being pharmacies, only seven, but their business is quite good. The most numerous are cigarette shops, with 105, indicating the large number of Lianmin who have a smoking habit. The officers and soldiers of the entire 63rd Division stationed there, as well as all the staff of the Commissioner's Office and the county government, have all quit smoking cigarettes to promote the anti-smoking campaign. Since September 1st, the import of cigarettes has been strictly prohibited to eliminate the bad habits of the people. Most of the tobacco leaves, tin foil, and cardboard used for cigarettes are imported, and many of the manufacturing companies are run by foreign merchants. By advocating a hundred effects and prohibiting them, it is not only of great benefit to national health.

Suzhou

Factional Disputes in the Women's Association

The Wuxian Women's Association was initially initiated by Chen Suwu and others, and then by Kong Meizhi and others. After mediation by the county party headquarters, they merged and organized. However, internal factional disputes were fierce and uncompromising until now, when they barely managed to complete the organization. It was scheduled to elect cadres yesterday (15th) afternoon and hold an inaugural meeting today (16th). Unexpectedly, when the membership meeting was held yesterday, the number of members present was insufficient to meet the quorum. Although instructor Chen Qian tried his best to rally them, it was unsuccessful and the meeting had to be declared adjourned. It is feared that it will be difficult to establish it in the near future.

Confiscation of Weights and Measures Leads to Market Strike

In the East Gate of Wujiang County, a market strike occurred on the previous day (14th) due to the inspection of weights and measures. According to investigations, a weights and measures inspector named Ni Jingfu, together with the county chamber of commerce and the Public Security Bureau, sent personnel to conduct inspections on that day. Initially, order was good in the city. However, when they reached Shengjiaku, they discovered old weights and measures on the winter vegetable stalls, which were taken away. Unexpectedly, the stallholders snatched them back and broke them, leading to a misunderstanding. All the shops went on strike in solidarity. Later, the county chamber of commerce, the county government, and the Public Security Bureau came forward to persuade them, and they resumed business as usual.

Wuxi

Barbers Have Resumed Work

The Laomeirongxuan Barber Shop and the Meihua Barber Shop outside Guangfu Gate on Hanchang Road, without the approval of their peers, lowered prices to attract customers, which led to opposition from the industry's workers. They all went on strike and smashed the goods and property of the Laomeirongxuan and Meihua barber shops. The Second Branch Bureau arrested Zhang Rongfu and 12 others and sent them to the General Bureau for interrogation and detention. Their actions had been misguided. It is learned that after this incident, the Barber Industry Association Zhou Shaoqin and others specifically presented a petition to the county government requesting the release of the arrested workers and requesting the maintenance of industry regulations. Over two hundred striking workers also held a meeting at the Bayierzhaohui to discuss ways to rescue the arrested workers. Tan Jinchun, Shen Deshan, Zhang Yusheng, Wu Aisheng, and four others were elected as representatives to lead over a hundred workers, holding flags, to petition the county party headquarters. Mao, the training officer of the headquarters, received them and agreed to forward the petition to the committee for review. They then petitioned the county government, where County Magistrate Yan received them personally. The representatives presented their petition and personally delivered the petition, requesting relief. Magistrate Yan gave them earnest advice, ordering them to resume work first to avoid losses. The arrested workers, except for those who had indeed engaged in destructive actions, should be detained for investigation, and the rest, if no major relationship was found, should be released on bail. Sha Licai and Liu Dabai were found to have violated industry regulations by lowering prices without authorization, which was improper. The Public Security Bureau was ordered to order them to restore the original price and not to disobey. The representatives were satisfied and dispersed. The arrested workers were tried in court by Section Chief Wu of the Public Security Bureau. As a result, eight people including Zhang Jidong were released on bail because they were unrelated. Zhang Rongfu and five others were found to have engaged in destructive actions and were ordered to be returned to custody. Yesterday (15th) morning at around 7:00, the barber shops inside and outside the city, in order to avoid unnecessary losses, resumed business first. However, the workers' side, because five workers were not allowed to be released, insisted on continuing the strike to show their determination. The county party headquarters and the county government, fearing that unscrupulous people would take the opportunity to cause trouble, in addition to ordering public security agencies to strictly guard against it, also sent responsible personnel to persuade the barber workers to resume work that day and wait for the official authorities to handle it fairly. By noon at 12:00, all the barber shops had resumed business and were operating as usual.

Night Sailing Boat Robbed in Panfeng

A night sailing boat owned by Feng Heyuan, which regularly travels from this county to Huangshan Bridge in Changzhou County, was robbed. On the evening of the day before yesterday, at 8 PM, while sailing from Wuxi to Changzhou as usual, the boat was passing the mulberry fields on the shore of Panfeng in this county when suddenly seven bandits armed with flashlights and pistols emerged. They seized the two crew members who were pulling the boat from the shore, forced them to pull the boat closer to the bank, jumped aboard, silenced everyone, and looted at will. After about half an hour, they left with their stolen goods. Afterwards, the boat owner, Feng Heyuan, inspected his losses and found that tin foil, foreign yarn, cloth, fruit, clothing, etc., worth over three hundred yuan, had been stolen. Currently, Feng Heyuan has reported the robbery to the shipping industry association, which has forwarded it to the county government, requesting the arrest of the thieves and the recovery of the stolen goods.

Jiangyin

Shanghai Police Come to Cheng to Arrest Runaway Wife

Yu Wenlin, a box and brush maker from 7 Jishan Street, Nanshi, Shanghai, had a wife named Sun, who was enticed away by Liu Laigen (who worked in the same factory) from Yejimiao, Waihu Bridge, Chengxi. Liu took Sun and three to four thousand yuan worth of clothing and jewelry to Cheng, lodging in the Su residence in Chayuan Alley, West Main Street. Yu Wenlin reported this to the First Police Station of the Second District of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau. They arrested Liu Laigen and sent police officers to Cheng on the 13th to cooperate with the Public Security Bureau's detective team in arresting Sun. However, she had already heard the news and fled.

Nantong

Flood Victims Along the River Appeal for Dyke Repair

The dike along the Yangtze River in the Langshan District of Nantong was breached by river tides, causing a disastrous flood. The breach has not yet been repaired. Currently, the dikes of Baizhang and other areas are being severely eroded and are in danger of collapsing into the river at any moment. The flood victims are now appealing to the county government to quickly purchase firewood and stones and rush to carry out emergency repair work to protect against the river tides.

Rugao

Burglary Occurs in Yangmu Township

Liu Qingyun, a resident of Yangmu Township in the urban area, is a well-to-do owner of a general store. The night before last, eight bandits speaking with mixed accents, dressed in short clothes, and armed with flashlights and box cannons, scaled the wall and entered his house. They first tied up the store staff and family members, then rummaged through boxes and chests. At that moment, the rope binding Liu suddenly loosened, and he took the opportunity to escape and shout for help. The bandits, realizing they could not stay long, howled and fled. Afterwards, an inspection revealed that over two hundred yuan in cash, seven taels of gold jewelry, and a pair of pearl hairpins were missing. The incident has already been reported to the district office for investigation and pursuit.

Yangzhou

Shop Assistants in Six Trades Oppose the Expansion of the Dasheng Incident

In Yangzhou City, six trades including silk, cloth, Western clothing, and Gu embroidery are opposing the business dispute of Dasheng Silk Bureau. Labor and management have been on strike and the market has been closed for three days. As the incident expands, repeated mediation has failed. Dasheng Silk Bureau has scheduled its reopening for the 14th. Upon hearing this news, hundreds of shop assistants from the six trades formed a team at dawn, lined up in front of Dasheng’s gate, each holding small flags and distributing hunger strike declarations. This prevented Dasheng from reopening. At one point, thousands of onlookers gathered. The Public Security Bureau and the county chamber of commerce sent dozens of police and business group members to stand guard in front of Dasheng's gate, alongside the six trades, to provide assistance. They organized a comfort team for the six trades, providing them with steamed buns to satisfy their hunger. Wang Lu, a representative from the provincial party headquarters, arrived in Yangzhou to investigate the dispute and, together with County Magistrate Ma, Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang, and Lawyers Association Dai Tianqiu, went to Dasheng at 2 PM to persuade the bureau to postpone its reopening. They also persuaded the shop assistants from the six trades to disperse and await a meeting of all relevant parties to be convened tomorrow (the 15th) to discuss a proper solution. Both sides accepted the proposal, and the shops dispersed.

Huzhou

Bandits Rob Sailing Boat in Broad Daylight

Near Nanggao Bridge, about ten li outside the North Gate of Wuxing, a sailing boat owner named Zhou Anian was carrying seventeen passengers yesterday at around 7 AM, heading to Huzhou. While passing the Dragon King Temple, a person from Henan claimed to want to board the boat. The sailing boat immediately docked. After the bandit got off the boat, it turned out that there were already three bandits disguised as passengers on board. They each pulled out a pistol, first robbing passenger Qian Lu’s two gold rings and a pair of gold bracelets, as well as over a hundred yuan in cash from her pocket. Then, they robbed all the silver, silk, and other items carried by the passengers and fled.

The fifth annual meeting of the Zhejiang branch of the National Private Electricity Industry Association was held in Shaoxing. The Daming Company prepared in advance. Robbery of Cargo Ship Injures Two Crew Members

At the Shuixian Temple near Huiqian in Nanxiang on the 13th at midnight, a cargo ship sailing from Linpu to Shaoxing was forced to stop by five bandits on the shore. Local News

Cotton Industry Control Committee Officially Established Today, Presided Over by Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the Economic Council, Ceremony Simple, No Foreign Guests Invited

The National Economic Council’s Cotton Industry Control Committee, after the National Government appointed Chen Jiangfu and twenty others as members and designated Chen Guangfu as Chairman, immediately began preparations for organization, renting the sixth floor of the Continental Building at 10 Jiujiang Road as its headquarters. The establishment ceremony will be held today (the 16th) at 10 AM, with all members present at the headquarters. Chen did not want extravagance, so apart from inviting the three standing committee members of the Economic Council to attend and deliver speeches, no foreign guests were invited. The establishment meeting will be presided over by Minister Song Ziwen. Details are as follows:

Setting Up Headquarters

The committee originally had a temporary office in the Shanghai Bank Building, but because the available space was insufficient, they rented rooms 603, 604, 605, 606, 607, and 608 on the sixth floor of the Continental Building at 10 Jiujiang Road as their headquarters. The area is quite large. The temporary office was moved in the day before yesterday, and the staff have been actively setting up the headquarters. Internal equipment is being installed busily. As of 5 PM yesterday, everything was set up.

Establishment Ceremony

The opening ceremony today will be very simple: (1) The chairman will respectfully read the Premier’s will; (2) A standing committee member of the National Economic Council will give a speech; (3) The chairman will give a speech; (4) The meeting will adjourn.

List of Committee Members

The list of committee members, as announced by the National Government, is as follows: Chen Guangfu, Li Shenbo, Liu Zuokai, Tang Xinghai, Zou Qiuwen, Chen Lifu, Rong Zongjing, Zhang Gongquan, Du Yuesheng, Pei Songsun, Zhang Xiaolin, Guo Shun, He Bingxuan, Hu Du'an, Liu Yinfei, Sun Enqing, Wu Xingya, Nie Lusheng, Mu Xiangyue, Chen Bozhuang, Li Haoju, and twenty-one others. Chen Guangfu was designated as the chairman.

Organizational Regulations

The Provisional Organizational Regulations of the National Economic Council's Cotton Industry Control Committee (approved by the National Government on October 7, 1933) Article 1: The National Economic Council, in order to improve and develop the national cotton and textile industries and rationalize them, establishes the Cotton Industry Control Committee in accordance with the provisions of Article 7 of the Organizational Regulations. Article 2: The Cotton Industry Control Committee has the power to guide, supervise, and implement control, rewards, and punishments over the national cotton and textile industries. Article 3: The Cotton Industry Control Committee shall have a number of members, appointed by the National Government upon nomination by the standing committee members of the National Economic Council from various sectors, including textile, cotton planting, and finance. Article 4: The Cotton Industry Control Committee shall have one chairman and five standing committee members, designated by the National Government from among the committee members upon nomination by the standing committee members of the National Economic Council. Article 5: For the purpose of group research, the Cotton Industry Control Committee may establish four groups: economic, raw materials, manufacturing, and sales. Members of each group shall be appointed by the chairman. Article 6: The members of the Cotton Industry Control Committee and the members of each group shall serve as honorary positions. Article 7: The Cotton Industry Control Committee shall have a general affairs section to handle documents, accounting, and general affairs. Article 8: The Cotton Industry Control Committee shall have a technical section to design and research the following matters: 1. Matters concerning the improvement and promotion of cotton planting; 2. Matters concerning the organization, equipment, and management of textile factories; 3. Matters concerning the manufacture of textile machinery and its accessories; 4. Matters concerning the transportation and sale of cotton, cotton yarn, and their manufactured products; 5. Matters concerning the standardization of market transactions in the cotton and textile industries; 6. Matters concerning the study of tax regulations in the cotton and textile industries; 7. Matters concerning labor welfare facilities in the cotton and textile industries; 8. Matters concerning financial adjustments in the cotton and textile industries; 9. Matters concerning the training of personnel in the cotton and textile industries; 10. Matters concerning investigation and statistics in the cotton and textile industries; 11. Matters concerning the promotion of the cotton industry cooperative system; 12. Matters concerning other cotton and textile industries. Article 9: The general affairs section shall have one chief and six to ten staff members. The technical section shall have one chief and fifteen to twenty technical specialists, appointed or reappointed by the chairman upon nomination by the National Economic Council. Article 10: The Cotton Industry Control Committee may employ staff members as necessary for its work. Article 11: The Cotton Industry Control Committee shall hold a regular meeting once a week, and temporary meetings shall be held irregularly, both convened by the chairman. Article 12: Decisions of the Cotton Industry Control Committee shall be implemented by the chairman or handled by the National Economic Council. Article 13: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of approval by the National Government.

National Economic Council to Hold Plenary Session This Week to Discuss All Action Plans

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the National Government has already passed through the Central Political Council the appointments of twenty-nine members of the National Economic Council: Huang Shaoxiong, Gu Mengyu, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Gongbo, Wang Shijie, Zhang Renjie, Kong Xiangxi, Li Shizeng, Cai Yuanpei, Shao Yuanchong, Li Ming, Zhou Zuoming, Yu Qiaqing, Wu Shengchang, Rong Zongjing, Rui Heng, Chen Lifu, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Guangfu, Liu Hongsheng, Shi Liangcai, Xu Xinliu, Wang Kemin, Chen Bozhuang, Chu Minyi, Yang Duanliu, Qin Fen, Ye Gongchuo, Lian Shenghai, etc. It is reported that the three standing committee members of the council, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and Song Ziwen, plan to hold a plenary committee meeting in Nanjing this week to discuss all action plans. National Exhibition Closed Yesterday, Temporary Market Completely Ended, Certificates of Award Issued for Excellent Products

The National Products Movement Exhibition, organized by the Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of Shanghai and the China National Products Manufacturers' Federation, held its closing ceremony yesterday at 3 PM. About 500 representatives and guests from all walks of life attended, and awards were presented by Lin Guihou. Details are as follows:

Attending Representatives

The representatives from various sectors who attended yesterday included: Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hongen (represented by Li Zemin), Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Ye Jiaxing, Citizens' Association Lin Kanghou, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yilu, Chen Binghui, Liu Zhongying, Wang Chuang'e, Cao Zhigong, Chen Jicheng, Tao Leqin, Xu Guanghua, Zheng Dongshan, Zhu Zhichun, representatives from Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory, Yabuer Electric Bulb Factory, Meiya Silk Weaving Factory, Dalong Woolen Fabric Factory, Jinglun Cotton Thread Factory, Junyi Anti-Both Cloth Factory, May 30th Knitting Factory, Jinjing Necktie Company, Liang Xinji Toothbrush Factory, Shengda Woolen Weaving Factory, Stenhouse Beef Juice Company, Guanshengyuan, Dacheng Woolen Weaving Factory, and over 500 other representatives.

Chairman's Report

The presidium, consisting of Lin Kanghou, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yiqing, Chen Binghui, Liu Zhongying, Tao Leqin, Cao Zhigong, Chen Jicheng, and Ye Jiaxing, performed the rituals. Cao Zhigong then reported, saying: "Today is the closing ceremony of the National Products Exhibition. The exhibition period was originally set for three weeks, but was extended by ten days at the request of various sectors, totaling one month. During this month, although we dare not say that the results are excellent, we have certainly been able to move a portion of the public. Since the opening, over tens of thousands of compatriots have come to visit, showing that they have already felt the interest in promoting national products. Economic Expert Xu Peikun Discusses the Issue of Controlled Economy

The term "controlled economy" has been very popular recently, echoing the emergence of various new terms in the past, with different approaches but similar results. After a considerable period of time, the people who advocated them all disappeared without a trace. In reality, of course, there were no results. This phenomenon can be said to be our country's unique common problem. Whenever we want to start something, everyone is excited and enthusiastic, but when it comes to the point where there is no way to do it, needless to say, we just muddle through. Now, the whole country is happily advocating a controlled economy, and the people of the whole country naturally hope that this thing will succeed, so that after the controlled economy is realized, industry and commerce can develop greatly and the government will have the power to solve the problem of people's livelihood. What is frightening is that we may repeat the same mistakes, as if we only hear the sound of footsteps on the stairs but don't see anyone coming down. Speaking of the term "controlled economy," it is new in writing, so it has aroused the interest of scholars, but it is actually an old term. Whether in ancient or modern times, in China or abroad, it can be boldly said that no country has not implemented a controlled economy. During the European War, the countries that participated in the war absolutely controlled all aspects of production, consumption, and distribution by the government. Even eating a piece of bread or buying a pound of rice had to be approved by the government. The current Soviet Russia, of course, adopts this method. Other countries also have many examples of control in peacetime. Banks, railways, exchanges, and all large enterprises are subject to government control and restrictions. Our country's advocacy of a controlled economy seems like a recent thing on the surface, but in reality, our country is an old hand at implementing a controlled economy. Since ancient times, the establishment of pawnshops, barbershops, teahouses, tofu shops, and other shops has been subject to the strict constraints of the government and the industry association. There must be a considerable distance between them on a street before they are allowed to open. The transportation and sale of rice, salt, and other consumer goods are also subject to strict supervision by the government. The opium problem is also within the same scope of prohibition. Sometimes the government also interferes with the entry and exit of copper coins. From this, it can be seen that the controlled economy is an old hand talking about everyday matters. The reason why this issue is being enthusiastically advocated today is probably because the problems of rice, wheat, cotton, etc., are too important, so we have paid attention to the issue of control. However, there have been several discussions on the problems of rice, wheat, cotton, etc., which all included the meaning of control. In summary, the method of controlled economy is not new, and all countries have it. What we should pay attention to is what the result will be after the implementation of the controlled economy. The meaning and responsibility of a controlled economy A controlled economy is an old method, as I said last time, but its scope and meaning depend on the size and nature of the enterprise. In simple terms, its meaning and responsibility are to make production, consumption, and distribution regular, so that people can get what they need, support themselves, stabilize social order, and make people live and work in peace. However, to achieve this goal and solve the problem of people's livelihood, we must first develop production, which requires everyone to have a job and receive considerable remuneration so that consumption can be smooth and distribution can be balanced. In this way, the controlled economy bears the mission of solving the entire problem of people's livelihood, which is certainly the most difficult thing. The Premier, in his Industrial Plan, stipulated that large enterprises should be state-owned and small enterprises should be privately owned, and also stipulated the method of equalizing land ownership, which are all problems of controlled economy, but when it comes to implementation, we feel many difficulties. The conditions for implementing a controlled economy A controlled economy bears the responsibility of solving the problem of people's livelihood, and its importance can be imagined. A controlled economy is an old method, but the result of its implementation is often contrary to expectations, and the difficulty of implementing control is also clear. The failure of modern industry and commerce to develop and the fact that the national economy is in a desperate situation clearly prove that our country has no unified method and urgently needs to find an overall control strategy that encompasses everything. However, this strategy is originally a very easy thing when it is just a paper talk, but in reality, it is a very difficult thing to do it step by step, so that it can play a role, have an effect, and consistently reach the destination. In simple terms, if we want the controlled economy to produce effective results, we must first have all kinds of conditions. However, these conditions are very difficult to present in full, because there are many gaps between words and facts, which cannot be expressed. Now, I will list seven conditions for reference: (1) Correct facts; (2) Proper theoretical basis; (3) Thorough economic and commercial knowledge; (4) Experienced professionals in various industries; (5) Talents with enterprise design and management; (6) Talents for implementation; (7) Sufficient economic power.

Mr. Chen Yuxiu, an Overseas Chinese in Batavia, Discusses the General Situation of Domestic Goods in Nanyang: Six Major Reasons for the Sluggish Sales of Domestic Goods, and Hopes That Domestic Goods Merchants Will Pay Close Attention

In order to thoroughly investigate whether domestic goods are suitable for sale in Nanyang, Mr. Chen Baipeng, a Chinese businessman in Batavia, Nanyang, specially sent Mr. Chen Yuxiu to Shanghai. A reporter from the New Voice Society interviewed him yesterday at his residence and recorded the following conversation to inform those who are concerned about Nanyang trade. The reporter asked, "I heard that overseas Chinese in Nanyang are affected by the global economic downturn, and their economies are declining. What is the current situation?" Mr. Chen replied, "The decline of Chinese businesses in the Dutch East Indies is due to the instability of their economic foundation. Although some people say that the reason for this instability is the lack of large enterprises such as banks, I believe that the reason for the failure of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies is that the position they occupy in commerce is not healthy. Because overseas Chinese are all intermediaries, they sell manufactured goods to consumers (natives) and sell raw materials from producers (natives) to capitalists. Now, the level of knowledge of the natives has increased, and capitalists have become more emotionally connected due to their long-term association with the natives, so all transactions are directly sold without the need for overseas Chinese as intermediaries. This is the reason for the decline of overseas Chinese. If we want to save overseas Chinese in the future, the only way is to make overseas Chinese merchants selling domestic goods, rather than intermediaries who specialize in buying and selling goods for foreign capitalists. Only then will the commercial power of overseas Chinese have a day of revival." Asked how the strength of Japan in Nanyang compares to that of overseas Chinese, he replied, "In theory, economic decline is a universal phenomenon, and the Japanese should also be affected. However, the fact is beyond expectations. The Japanese business in the Dutch East Indies is not only not declining, but is flourishing. What is the reason for this? Because at least 80% of the suppliers of various manufactured products in the two oceans market are Japanese. Except for those who operate in local products, most of the overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies are distributors of Japanese goods. These overseas Chinese who distribute Japanese goods are gradually in danger of being eliminated. Because the Japanese have learned from the domestic and overseas Chinese boycott movement, since September 18th, they have imitated overseas Chinese and opened small grocery stores everywhere, specializing in selling Japanese goods directly to the natives. The power of overseas Chinese is gradually unsustainable." Asked how the sales of domestic goods in the Nanyang market are, he replied, "It is very shameful to say that there are more than 1.3 million overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies, but Chinese goods account for only 2-3%. The Japanese have only five or six thousand people, but Japanese goods almost dominate the entire market. This is because Japanese goods are dumped at low prices and penetrate everywhere. It is not that overseas Chinese do not work hard to promote domestic goods in Nanyang. First, Chinese industry is backward, and only in recent years has there been a vigorous atmosphere, but the Nanyang market has been preempted by Japanese goods. Second, the industrial center of China is unfortunately in Shanghai, and most of the overseas Chinese are from Fujian and Guangdong, and they are not familiar with the situation in Shanghai. If the factories are located in Xiamen, Guangzhou, or Hong Kong, domestic goods will definitely be able to go there more. For example, dry batteries, cotton yarn shirts, etc. produced in Hong Kong have considerable sales in Nanyang. Third, Shanghai factories have always rarely sent people to Nanyang to promote goods, and even if people go, they are less effective because of language barriers and unfamiliarity with the local conditions in Nanyang. Fourth, Shanghai manufacturers do not pay much attention to the goods shipped to Nanyang, which causes distributors to suffer significant losses, and Shanghai manufacturers are often greedy for small immediate profits and do not pay attention to the quality of the goods. For example, umbrellas have a large sales volume in the Dutch East Indies, but Shanghai manufacturers did not pay attention. After shipping lacquer to oil umbrellas to Java, the lacquer melted due to the hot weather, making it difficult to open. Therefore, the sales of Shanghai umbrellas have gradually been seized by Japanese umbrellas. Fifth, Chinese merchants do lack some patriotism. They often pass off Japanese goods as domestic goods. For example, 3G and 3K shirts were originally very popular in Java, but some overseas Chinese who were blinded by profit sent samples to Japan to imitate them. Because Japanese prices are cheaper, the market is disrupted. Sixth, Nanyang lacks some publicity for domestic goods. If more domestic goods exhibitions are held, overseas Chinese will naturally pay attention to domestic goods. Secondly, more domestic goods stores should be opened so that overseas Chinese have the opportunity to buy domestic goods, because there are very few businesses that are completely engaged in domestic goods business." Asked about his opinion on the promotion of domestic goods, he replied, "The most important thing is not to be greedy for small immediate profits, improve the quality of goods, and pay attention to publicity work. Then the promotion of domestic goods will definitely be very smooth." Finally, according to Mr. Chen, he has been introduced by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and has visited many factories. If other factories want to promote goods in Nanyang, they can contact the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Commodity Exhibition Center to help them contact.

The Silk Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Held a Meeting Yesterday to Request Funding for the Establishment of a Rayon Factory

The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Joint Association convened industry leaders from the two provinces yesterday for an emergency meeting to discuss fundamental ways to save the silk industry. Representatives from silk industry associations in various districts of the two provinces attended, including Shi Yunqing, Ma Yangshi, Yu Wenqing, and Mo Yong from Suzhou; Wang Wuquan and Zhao Fuzhong from Hangzhou; Wang Jiean, Wang Xingyi, Wu Niannong, and Xu Wenbing from Shanghai; Shen Tingquan from Shaoxing; Shen Tonghua and Wu Xingcheng from Huzhou; Wang Shihua from Danyang; and dozens of others. The meeting began at 3:30 PM, and Wang Jiean was elected as the chairman. The chairman announced the purpose of the meeting and read out the proposals from various districts, which were discussed one by one. (1) The proposal from the Wuxian Gauze and Satin Industry Association stated that the business of domestic real silk satin was sluggish and declining, while foreign and domestic rayon fabrics were beautiful and attractive, catering to the psychology of women, so sales were better than real silk fabrics. As a result, European and American countries imported tens of millions of yuan worth of rayon into China every year. Such a huge outflow urgently needs to be saved, otherwise, the people will be poor and the wealth will be exhausted, which is deeply concerning. If China bans rayon, then silk will definitely disappear, and foreign silk will take the opportunity to invade, and the outflow will be ten times greater than today. Fortunately, the US cotton loan has been successful and has been decided by the Central Political Conference to be used for productive enterprises. Based on this reason, it is proposed to petition the National Government to approve a part of the cotton and wheat loan to establish a rayon factory to stop the outflow and save the silk industry from danger. After discussion, everyone agreed that the price of rayon in the East Neighbor (Japan) is only half of that in Jiangsu and Zhejiang because there are no taxes, so the price of Japanese silk is also cheaper than that of China. If China uses Western rayon, the cost of making silk will be more expensive than Japanese silk due to high import duties. How can it compete with Japanese silk? Therefore, if we do not set up our own rayon factory and only use Western rayon, not only will the outflow be very large, but also although the silk factory will be able to stand, the result is a consensus to petition the National Government to approve the allocation of 20 million yuan of cotton and wheat loans to establish a rayon factory to save profits and save from danger. Secondly, the discussion of the Hangzhou representatives requested that the silk industry be saved. After careful discussion by the representatives, everyone agreed that Western-style clothing is now popular, and all use foreign goods, and even children wear Western-style clothing, and most of the Chinese robes and jackets also use foreign goods such as foreign silk. No wonder the domestic silk cloth is so decadent. If we do not urgently seek to save it, we will all wear foreign goods. It was decided that (1) industry regulations should be rectified and production should be controlled to avoid oversupply and self-defeat; (2) the association should notify the local silk satin industry associations to inform all colleagues to wear domestic clothing; (3) the Executive Yuan should be submitted to reinstate the previous order to restrict civil servants to wear domestic goods; (4) the Ministry of Education should be requested to order the national education bureaus to strictly prohibit teachers and students in all schools from wearing Western-style clothing, and all should wear domestic clothing except for gymnastics; (5) manufacturing methods should be improved; (6) the Yuanbu should be requested to temporarily exempt rayon import duties before rayon is produced in China, and then add heavy taxes to foreign goods after there are domestic goods; (7) more domestic goods companies should be established so that there are stores that specialize in selling domestic goods and stop the dumping of foreign goods.

The Central Government Exempts Business Tax on Cotton Receiving Offices and Branch Offices of Yarn Factories

Since the implementation of business tax in various provinces, all cotton receiving offices and branch offices of yarn factories are also subject to the tax, which is inconsistent with the unified tax regulations. Exemptions have been applied for many times and disputes have lasted for years. Recently, Xie Zuokai, Tang Xinghai, Li Shengbo and others, members of the Cotton Industry Control Committee, negotiated with the authorities, and the central government and provincial governments have agreed to approve the exemption. The original text of the central government's reply is disclosed below. According to the petition submitted to the Ministry by representatives of the Chinese Yarn Factory Association, the yarn factory office is the agency representing the yarn factory, which is the same as the Da Zhonghua Firecracker Company case, and its cotton receiving office is the agency representing the yarn factory collecting raw materials, which is the same nature as the flour factory purchasing wheat. It is requested to be exempted from business tax. After investigation, if the branch offices of each yarn factory engage in the sale of cotton yarn (regardless of whether it is produced by the factory) or other goods, according to the provisions of the first item of the interpretation method in the Ministry's previous advisory to the provinces and cities, business tax should still be levied. However, if the branch offices of each yarn factory are only responsible for contacting and transferring on behalf of the factory, and do not have the nature of sales and marketing, and have no business income, and the branch office has been approved by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for registration, it can submit the registration and the relevant supporting documents of the nature of the business and submit it to the Ministry to instruct the competent authority to verify the facts again, and then it can be exempted in accordance with the Da Zhonghua Firecracker Company branch office case. As for the original petition, the cotton receiving offices set up by yarn factories are also the agencies representing the yarn factories to collect raw materials, and have no business behavior, which is the same nature as the flour factories purchasing wheat, which is still the actual situation. In order to rescue the yarn industry and take care of the difficulties of merchants, the Ministry has approved the method for exempting each yarn factory's cotton receiving office from buying cotton raw materials. First, each yarn factory must be registered with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the cotton receiving office set up directly buys cotton, which is indeed only for the raw materials of the factory's textile, and has no sales business behavior, and does not concurrently operate other goods. A certificate is issued by the local Chamber of Commerce, and the competent levy authority verifies the agreement, and business tax should be exempted. Second, if there is a shadow enterprise license number, set up a village number to buy in the place of origin, or other merchants operating cotton, in order to prevent sales and profit, and take the opportunity to steal and leak, business tax should still be levied to show restrictions. According to the previous situation, in addition to the distribution and approval, Xiangying Advisory request for verification, instruct the competent authorities to verify and comply with the one-size-fits-all, and prevent disputes. This consults the provincial and municipal governments.

Sino-German Joint Venture to Establish Aircraft Manufacturing Plant. The Amount of Capital is Set at Three Million Yuan, to be Held After Approval by Both Parties

The Daily News reports that after China was repeatedly devastated and oppressed by the Japanese air force in the September 18th and January 28th incidents, it has been promoting air defense with all its strength. The voice of aviation saving the country has spread throughout the country. The government and the aviation authorities deeply feel that the development of the aviation industry is not easy because China currently does not have an aircraft manufacturing plant. The amount of capital is temporarily set at 3 million yuan, divided into 7,000 shares. China will hold two-thirds, and Germany will hold one-third. The contract is being drafted, and after approval by the governments of both parties, it will be held to select a location.

The Lawyers Association's Autumn General Meeting Failed to Achieve a Quorum Yesterday, Changed to a Discussion Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its autumn general meeting yesterday (Sunday) at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association Auditorium on Xizang Road in the Public Concession. The members present were Shen Junru, Zhi Chi, Wu Guotai, Wang Weizhen, Yan Yinwu, Chen Tingrui, Liu Xiang, Li Yuan, Yao Jian, Yu Zufeng, Shi Qinghua, Zhou Shiying, Zhu Fuju, Mao Yun, Liu Shiqi, Zhang Shewo, Chen Zhigao, Zhang Zhengxue, Shen Qichang, Cai Nipei, Le Fen, Lei Guoneng, Xiong Chuyin, Yang Zhi, Li Caixia, Liang, Qian Longsheng, Wu Peng, Peng Qixiu, etc., a total of one hundred and ten people. At 3:30 PM, the meeting was opened by ringing the bell. Shen Junru, Wang Weizhen, Chen Tingrui, and other three standing members were publicly elected as the presidium, and Dai Jixian recorded. The meeting was held as usual. After Chairman Shen Junru reported that the association had a total of one thousand and forty members, according to the legal number, there must be two hundred and sixty-one members present to meet the legal number. He had to change the meeting to a discussion meeting. The procurators withdrew first because the meeting failed to achieve a quorum. The details of the meeting are summarized as follows: (1) Reporting items: (A) Shen Junru reported on general affairs, (B) Chen Tingrui reported on accounting, (C) Wang Weizhen reported on documents. (2) Proposals: (A) Member Yao Jian proposed to oppose the collection of lawyer delivery fees, (B) Member Wang Enji proposed to request the city's courts to allow bail to be found in any regional court area for reports of detention in the future, (C) The Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions requested assistance for the case of the telephone company in the Concession oppressing workers, (D) Member Hu Chongji proposed that the Special District Court's public prosecution cases against the patrol room are entirely based on the patrol room's intentions, which is unfair, (E) Member Liu Xiang proposed that the court does not notify the parties when announcing public judgments when the parties are detained, and requested correction, (F) Member Pan Xi proposed to transfer a letter to the court that duplicate copies must be written in ink in the future, (G) Member Wang Zengxian proposed to forward the case to the Ministry of Judicial Administration and quickly send someone to investigate the central government's order to vigorously implement bail. After the original proposers made their reasons for the proposals, the chairmen Shen Junru, Chen Tingrui, Wang Weizhen, members Yao Jian, Hu, Liu Xiang, Cai Nipei, etc. expressed their opinions to each other. As a result, it was decided to submit the proposals to the Reporting and Supervision Committee for discussion at the meeting. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned at 5:30 PM.

Public Memorial for Wang Leping Yesterday

The coffin of Mr. Wang Leping, a member of the Central Committee, was transported back to his native Shandong yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM and publicly buried at the eastern foot of Qianfo Mountain. The Central Committee and all walks of life believed that Wang had made significant contributions to the revolution during his lifetime. Therefore, a public memorial was held at the Shandong Guild Hall on Jinji Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. Wang Faqin, a member of the Central Committee, presided over the memorial. After the memorial, the coffin was moved to Longhua Station, and the railway bureau prepared a car to transport it back to his hometown. The details are divided as follows:

Venue Arrangement

Please remember that where the road is sloping and there is an earthen road intersection, a white bamboo cloth banner inscribed with "Public Memorial for Mr. Wang Leping and Others" will be hung. From there southward to the Shandong Guild Hall, route signs will be placed along the way. At the entrance of the Shandong Guild Hall, a plain white archway will be erected, with a plaque in the middle stating "Public Memorial for Mr. Wang Leping." On the sides, memorial couplets will be hung, reading "The Spirit Never Dies, Righteousness Endures." After entering the main gate, memorial couplets will cover all four walls. In the center of the hall, a portrait of Mr. Wang will be hung, and various floral wreaths donated by different sectors will be placed before the spirit.

Holding of the Public Memorial

Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, the public memorial ceremony was held. Central Committee member Wang Faqin presided over the ceremony, and the municipal Public Security Bureau Military Band played funeral music. Following this, floral wreaths and libations were offered, and the presiding officer read the memorial oration. Afterward, a representative of Mr. Wang's family delivered a response. After the public memorial, the coffin was moved to Longhua Station, where the Railway Bureau provided a train for transportation. On the morning of the 16th at 10 AM, another public memorial ceremony will be held at Xiaguan Station in Nanjing. Afterward, a special Jinpu Railway train will be used for transport, and it is expected to arrive in Jinan on the morning of the 18th. Central Party Headquarters representative Ding Weifen and Shandong Province Governor Han Fuqu will conduct the welcoming ceremony at Jinan Station. That afternoon, a public memorial will be held at Zhongshan Park.

A Glimpse of Memorial Couplets

Many important figures from the Party and the nation have sent memorial couplets. Excerpts are as follows: (Wang Faqin) "Why did you kill the gentleman? Ten thousand miles to summon the soul, hearing night cries. How many shared hardship and adversity? For three years, buried bones have green mountains." (Kong Xiangxi) "Twenty years of striving for the nation, arduously and fortunately, yet a virtuous and heroic man has fallen. The sound of the Huangpu River tide still sobs. Three times, across the miles, he returns for burial, forever cherishing his heroism, while the mountains of Que and Hua stand majestically." (Wu Tiecheng) "Thirty years of distinguished service, his reputation still lingers in Licheng. One morning, a shocking tragedy, how much weeping and mourning for Jiangnan." (Li Liejun) "Such rivers and mountains, difficult for those who die later. A lifetime of brilliance, alas, a departed martyr."

Public Memorial Oration

On this 15th day of October, in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, we respectfully offer clear wine and simple dishes to the spirit of Mr. Wang Leping, saying: At the foot of Mount Tai, a unique spirit flourishes. Mr. Wang obtained it and was capable of great fearlessness. Dedicating himself to revolution for thirty years, he was not swayed by material possessions, and his integrity grew stronger. He once penetrated deep into enemy strongholds alone, remaining calm, facing life and death. Residing in Shanghai, he advocated democracy, offending the world's taboos, his blood flowing on the riverbanks. Our beautiful rivers and mountains are half-submerged by foreign powers. National humiliation and great disgrace to the nation. The times are deteriorating day by day, cause for lamentation. The dead are gone; what can the living redeem? Alas, may you enjoy this offering.

Zhan Jifeng Appointed Legal Advisor to the Garrison Command

Wu, the concurrently serving Commander of the Songhu Garrison, yesterday appointed lawyer Zhan Jifeng as legal advisor to the Command. It is reported that Mr. Zhan is a renowned lawyer in Shanghai. Since Commander Qian Dajun was in charge of the Songhu Garrison in the 17th year of the Republic, he admired Mr. Zhan's reputation and appointed him as legal advisor. When Commander Xiong Tianyi succeeded him, he continued to retain Mr. Zhan. For several years, his contributions were remarkable. Mr. Zhan resigned due to illness last spring, and the position remained vacant since then. Now, Commander Wu, who is also the mayor, believes that as the Garrison is transferring criminals to the concession courts, a representative with profound legal knowledge and familiarity with the concession agreements is needed to be competent. Since Mr. Zhan is currently serving as the legal advisor to the Municipal Public Security Bureau and is already familiar with the situation, he has been appointed concurrently as the legal advisor to the Garrison.

Participants

Among them, the "Heygendorff" Sacred Horse and the Indian Sacred Tiger, among other performances, were even more amazing and spectacular. The sound of applause never ceased. That wild beasts can be tamed to this extent, obeying human commands, is truly not easy.

Former Director of the Savings and Remittance Bureau Yang Jianping Accused The Control Yuan Filed an Impeachment The Special Court Prosecutor Filed a Public Prosecution Discrepancy of 150,000 in Payment Amount

Mr. Yang Jianping, the former Director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, was impeached by the Control Yuan for dereliction of duty and malfeasance. He was then transferred to the Central Public Functionary Disciplinary Committee for handling. The committee immediately investigated each of the Control Yuan's accusations. It was then discovered that Mr. Yang did indeed have significant suspicion of wrongdoing and should be strictly investigated by the Shanghai District Court according to the law. Yesterday, according to reliable sources, it was said that Mr. Yang was residing in Hong Kong due to illness and therefore could not appear in court on schedule. It is said that the most important point in this case is the discrepancy in the amount paid for the purchase of real estate, which amounts to a huge sum of 150,000 taels.

Pucao Road Begins Surveying

For the sake of convenient transportation in the Caojing and Pusong areas of western Shanghai, Yang Xinzheng and others, municipal committee members of the Caojing District, initiated the opening of Pucao Road, which starts from the west of Caohejing Town, passes through Huangjia Garden directly to Yaojiawan Bridge at the intersection of Pusong and Caojing Districts, and then turns north through Hongqiao Town to Chengjiaqiao on Hongqiao Road, with a total length of more than ten miles. However, the eastern section of Pucao Road was built by Huang Jinrong, a well-known figure in Shanghai, with his own funds and has been open to traffic for a long time. Due to the large scale of the western section and the tight municipal budget, it has not been implemented for the time being. Now, it is learned that the municipal government believes that the completion of the road is necessary for the development of traffic and commerce in western Shanghai.
