Free Talk

After the Transformation

— Ou Bi

It should be the time for transformation: your consciousness tells you so, and your environment forces you so. Thus, you transform. You discard all sighs that should not be sighed, tears that should not be shed. You have a new life. You are becoming a meaningful person, like George Sand.

Now, the first step of your work is to deeply study art, because art is the reflection of life, the crystallization of human suffering. After thoroughly studying art, you must bravely embark on the perilous path of life, singing generously, regarding death as homecoming, carving a path of blood from the midst of thorns and wild beasts for the sake of all humanity, to alleviate their suffering and tragically complete your own tragic life.

However, first, you must study the art that reflects your life. To study art, you must go to [Nanguo], because in [Nanguo], there is the yearning of your genius, the illusion of your ideal.

Naturally, when you decided to leave Shanghai and go to [Nanguo], you felt a nameless sense of melancholy, because [Haishang] is where you lingered, just as you are attached to West Lake. West Lake has tender affection, but [Haishang] has the vigor of resolute struggle; West Lake has the beauty of mountains and rivers, but [Haishang] has the majestic beauty of machinery; West Lake has... [Haishang] has... But what about [Nanguo]? Will you embark on your path of wandering again in this temporary respite? What kind of impression will [Nanguo] give you? Will it give you light, or...?

So you hesitate again, you waver again.

But in a flash, you say to yourself: What is there to hesitate about? What is there to waver about? Besides death, what else could there be? So you quickly organize your books and check your clothes as if you were determined to die.

Thus, like a warrior going to martyrdom, you march heroically to [Nanguo], to study the art of relieving human suffering and completing your own tragic life.

After [Feeling the Past]

— Feng Zhiyu

I still have a little more to write. But let me state beforehand that this is triggered by Mr. Shi Zhicun's words, but it is not written for him. In my original manuscript, I often mentioned the name of "Ge Chun", but when it was printed, it often turned into the word "[Mou]," or the common symbol "[XX]" for all the names of wealthy people, dangerous words, and vulgar terms for reproductive organs. I hope that some of the words in this article will not change like this, to avoid misunderstanding.

What I want to say now is: it is difficult to speak, and it is not easy not to speak. Those who wield the pen must always write articles, and once they write articles, they inevitably invite disaster. The water of the Yellow River attacks the weak dikes, so women with exposed arms and young people who write wrong characters become objects of ridicule. They are truly without strength or courage, and can only endure, just like villagers who go to the Shanghai Concession and have no choice but to be called "[Ah Mu Lin]".

However, some are wronged. Just to give an example, there is Mr. Liu Bannong's [Self-Annotated and Self-Approved] [Tonghua Zhidoutang Poetry Collection] in the 26th issue of [The Analects], a collection of doggerel poems. When Peking University was recruiting students, he was a grader. He found a ridiculous misspelling on a Chinese paper and wrote a poem about it. Those people who were criticized were so distressed that they wanted to burrow into the ground, those recent middle school graduates. Of course, he is a professor, and everything he points out cannot be wrong, but I think there is still room for discussion in some cases. There is a [Self-Annotation] in the collection that says: {

[Some wrote "Advocating Culture," and I said: "Advocating" is the word for "Prostitute." Wherever culture is developed, there must be many prostitutes, saying that culture is clarified by prostitutes, which is also logically sound.] We do not write "Prostitute's" "chang" as "advocating" now, but the two words were commonly used before. Mr. Liu is probably quoting from ancient books. But if you want to quote ancient books, I remember there is a sentence in [The Book of Songs] that says "Chang yu he nu," which does not seem to be interpreted as "I also became a prostitute to echo others." So that misspelling is just a mistake, ridiculous and contemptible, but it does not belong to him. There is also one named {

[Fortunately, [the buds of scientific thought] are sprouting,]

The word [sprouting] and the word [buds] both have a circle next to them, probably indicating that the laughable part is here, but I think [sprouts], [shoots], are certainly a noun, [budding], [germinating], become a verb,

During the May Fourth Movement, people advocated [Mr. Liu might interpret it as [raising prostitutes], people who write vernacular do not think it is strange to write a few wrong characters or use a few wrong classics, but because some opponents say that those who advocate vernacular are all people who do not know ancient books and speak nonsense, they often write a few sentences of classical Chinese to shut their mouths. But of course, because they come from the old camp, their accumulated habits are too deep, and they cannot get rid of them for a while, so it cannot be said that there are no authors with the breath of classical Chinese.

The vernacular movement of that time was victorious, and some warriors even climbed up because of this, but because they climbed up, they not only no longer fought for the vernacular, but also trampled it under their feet, took out ancient characters to laugh at the young people who came later. Because they are still using ancient books and ancient characters to laugh at people, some young people regard reading ancient books as an indispensable effort, and regard authors who often use classical Chinese as models to imitate, no longer trying to develop on new roads and create new situations.

There are two people here now: one is a student, who wrote [留學生] (liuxuesheng, international student) as [流學生] (liuxuesheng, wandering student) in the article, one wrong character; one is a university professor, who triumphantly wrote a poem, saying, [The teacher has committed a heinous crime, and is punished to go to the Western Paradise to make the learning flow. He should be the tenth class, boiling a pot of oil from exhausted gluten.] Let's see, which side is laughable?

Autumn Shade Notes 2 Shaoxing Wine Prices

— Yu Dafu

In Chinese notes, the price of wine in the Tang Dynasty is feared, and every time poems such as "three hundred bronze coins" or "fine wine ten thousand per dou" are used as answers, it is really unreliable, just like answering the source of the Yellow River with the three words "from the sky," which is the same. Now the most popular wine in China, which is excellent in color, aroma, and taste, is always Shaoxing wine, and the price of this Shaoxing wine is really strange, every household and every place is different. I don't know what it is like in Shaoxing City, but in places such as Beiping, Tianjin, Hankou, Nanjing, Guangzhou, and Shanghai, the price of wine varies due to the different places, which can still be said. Even in the same place, under the same wine name, the price sometimes goes up and down, which is really strange. Of course, the quality and quantity of the wine are another matter. According to my experience, Shaoxing wine in Hangzhou is indeed cheaper than elsewhere, this is in terms of quality and quantity. As for some hotels that hang up a sign of decades of Chen, which is a few yuan a catty at every turn, that is a deceptive talk. A few days ago, because of the rain, I had a big drunk at Yue's Tomb, and sang out, "Ten days of autumn shade, the water hits the sky, the lake and mountains are good but not allowed to fall, but with the extremely cheap Hangzhou wine, I am drunk in front of Xiling Yue's Tomb," which is also a real writing. Shaoxing wine from Dongpu and Ruan She is the best, other places. Although there are also workshops, the taste is always a little worse, probably because of the water.

Ganpu Correspondence (5)

— A Ying

Brother ○○··

These two days, we have been living in the salt fields' rise and decline, we have learned a lot about salt making. We who have always lived in the metropolis, once we enter this salt area, it is as if we have run into another world, everything is unfamiliar, everything is new. ］　［In the new　］, we gradually understand the difficulty of salt production, and in the land of salt, there have been many things that are worth our attention, such as the struggle between people and nature, and the hand-to-hand combat between people and wealthy gentry, like the endless sea waves, these things are constantly happening, in the past and in the present.

In order, let's talk about the production process of salt first. Salt, like rice, has fields, generally called [salt fields]; the so-called [salt production] is actually the beach where sea sprouts grow. Dividing these pure sandy beaches according to their width, they become one mu of field. The reason why they are divided horizontally instead of vertically is because the straightness grows towards the sea from time to time and cannot have any pattern. For each family or each mu of salt field, the salt farmers often plant a row of green grass at the boundary, which is probably the boundary marker. Such salt fields, when you drive past Zhapu, stretch along the coast: when you see a vast sea embankment, and there are protruding mounds of earth on the embankment, which look like graves from a distance, remember, this is the hometown of the salt you eat every day. When the tide comes, this kind of field is completely submerged in the water, and this is when the majestic sea plants salt in the salt farmers' fields. When the tide recedes, what is left for the salt farmers is a wet field, which the salt farmers are happy about. But salt does not succeed like this, after the tide comes, the salt farmers have to pin their hopes on the sky, they are eager for the arrival of strong sunlight. After a day of continuous sunshine, it always takes four or five days of continuous sunshine for the salt field to be completely sun-dried to white, and this white is the so-called salt. However, it must be continued for four or five days of sunshine, if it is sun-dried to the third or fourth day, and a burst of rain comes from the sky, and the rain reaches the size of dripping water on the eaves, then this time of sunshine is wasted, and the salt farmers, in addition to frustration, can only continue to wait for a few days, because the salt sun-dried to the soil surface is washed back into the soil by the rain. Even if it is sun-dried for four or five days, everyone has already shaved the ash and turned the soil, if it rains again, the work of turning the soil and shaving the ash is still without value. Therefore, after six or seven suns in a row, salt can be received: however, the procedure is not finished like this.

Regarding [shaving ash], we have to say a little more in detail. In the meantime, there are still many processes. When the sun has completely dried the salt to the soil surface, the salt farmers agree to shave it. Like the people working in the rice fields, they bring a lot of ash-shaving tools, and things like smoke and tea, and start working in the salt fields. Their first procedure is [shaving ash], the so-called [shaving ash] means scraping up the top layer of soil with a [shaving knife]. The [shaving knife] is a rectangular wooden frame about four or five feet long, with wood on three sides, and a cutting knife about one and a half feet long at the bottom. The salt farmer puts this on his head, holds both sides with both hands, the cutting knife penetrates into the soil, step by step, line by line, and drags it backward with great effort, so that the floating surface of the soil turns over under the edge of the knife, this is the soil with the most salt juice. After turning it over, let the sun dry it for another day and a half, and proceed to the next step of [pouring ash] work. [Pouring ash], the meaning of this is very easy to understand, that is, using a basket to pour this shaved soil into the salt pool. Speaking of [pouring ash], I have to conveniently, or even emphasize, to talk about the women in the salt field. In the salt field, in general, there are more female workers, they work very hard, and their results are often better than those of men, they do all aspects of the work in the process of salt making, [pouring ash] is also mostly done by them. They are as skilled in this aspect of work as men, and can quickly pour the ash into the basket, and when they pick it to the edge of the salt pool, they do not need to pour it one basket at a time, or have to put down the burden to pour it. They still stand straight, carry the ash on their shoulders, just pull the ropes at both ends and tilt, and all the ash in the two baskets falls into the pool. This way of pouring is what we usually see, but it is by no means an easy thing, so I specifically mention it here. This ash of the floating layer of soil is poured into the salt pool, but the procedure is not finished yet, followed by [picking water] [making brine] and other steps. For the sake of the　width,

In this letter, I cannot continue, I can only leave it for tomorrow. However, just based on the process that has been involved, it can be seen that the making of salt is not simple and difficult, and what is described here is only the matter of salt itself, only one-half of the production process. The ancient poem chanted rice, saying that rice is [every grain is hard work], if you understand the manufacturing process of salt, then how can salt not be obtained from blood and sweat?

Autumn Day (Continued)

— Jin Yi

A pale yellow face appeared, he remembered that healthy color, which had disappeared long ago; wrinkles were increasing in ones and twos. He held his chin with his hands, those hands, with blue veins that were even more prominent, it was not necessary to be surprised, but the sigh in his heart was born naturally.

Is it the fear of death, that is definitely not entirely true; he has long held hatred, and feels that there is nothing to miss in the current world. And the fear of middle age, the fear of old age, can be said to be people who are not afraid of winter, but they hate the mood of autumn.

He sat down on the chair, lit a cigarette and smoked, felt the prickly beard and felt that he should stand up and fix his face, but he collapsed again.

Sitting down on the ground, he thought to himself: [Isn't youth already gone]?

The servant who lightly opened the door showed a bit of panic standing there.

"You got up so early?"

He didn't answer just because he was too lazy to open his mouth. This old servant, watching him grow up since he was a child, seemed to be able to see his heart so clearly, so he didn't come to ask again.

"Shouldn't you wash your face?"

"Do you want to change clothes?"

He shook his head more vigorously, he seemed to hope that he could sit here alone, without a sound, so that the young memory could slowly crawl over. The old servant understood everything, so he lifted his steps lightly and retreated again.

He casually put his hand into the pocket of his pajamas, and his fingertip touched the slip of paper, and he remembered it immediately.

"People are really useless, how can I not remember anything?" He muttered.

Is it really that he doesn't remember? I'm afraid there hasn't been a moment in these fifteen years that he hasn't thought about her. And her shadow, as long as he closes his eyes, can flash out clearly, there is a small red mole there, there is a deep smile there, ···

Although he already knew what things were told to him inside, he still opened it and looked at it again, looking at her handwriting, which was said to be similar by a friend fifteen years ago, this has not changed. He can imagine what her posture should be when she writes, should there be a little twitch at the corner of her mouth? And he also remembers that the first time she picked up a pen in front of him, she covered it with one hand, with a naive shyness. And on that piece of paper it was written: On XX day, wait for me].

Is it attacked by a kind of joy, his hand is shaking slightly, and his eyes are a little blurry again, he wipes it with his hand, and tears are smeared evenly on his face.

Page 20

Special Supplement

Food Problems and Taxation

— Jun Da

It is a clear phenomenon that Chinese agriculture has declined in recent years, and rice production has also declined at the same time. However, the decline in rice production and the panic about food are generally regarded as the same thing, that is, the food panic is caused by the lack of rice production, which is really a vulgar argument. First, the phenomenon of food shortage in China is manifested in the import of foreign rice, but the import of foreign rice has only been a matter of the last thirty or forty years. In the past, except for special years such as famine years, China did not feel the lack of rice, nor did it need foreign rice to help. Therefore, the [natural productivity] of Chinese rice has not fallen behind the demand for rice, which is certain. Second, even if it is said that the [natural productivity] of Chinese rice is quite large, but the actual production has decreased in recent years, such as the conversion of rice fields to opium and raw material crops such as cotton, as well as the impact of man-made and natural disasters on harvests, that is also a fact. However, at the same time, along with the decrease in rice production, the proportion of rice in the diet of the Chinese people is further decreasing. Not only will the farmers in several northern provinces who eat rice disappear, but also the farmers in the central and southern regions who mainly use rice as their staple food, their staple food is gradually being replaced by inferior agricultural products such as sweet potatoes. Therefore, the food panic in China today caused by the lack of rice supply and the decline in food production are two completely different things. Otherwise, why is it that the good harvests of rice last year and today not only cannot solve the food panic problem, but also aggravate the degree of food panic, promoting the general farmers to go hungry, either as bandits or as starving people, to rob rice?

Therefore, promoting the decline of rice production is one thing, and forming a food panic is another. Sometimes, it is not the decline of rice production that causes the food panic, but the food panic that promotes the decline of rice production, such as the phenomenon of [good harvest turning into disaster], which is one aspect of this fact. This is a characteristic of the current social relations in China.

The reasons for promoting the food panic are very complicated, and one of the most important aspects is the [exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies] that have been the target of the national revolution in the past and now, and that have been shouted to be limited but have never been abolished. It can be simply explained by the following points:

First, the largest consumer market for rice in China today is obviously not the rural areas but the cities. The poverty of the peasant economy makes rice farmers have no rice to eat, and wheat farmers have no flour to eat. Rice production is not spread all over the country, but only limited to a few provinces. Therefore, the regulation of production and sales has become an important part of the food problem. The existence of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies hinders this important work. Not to mention the ban on rice exports from various provinces, but the heavy taxes are enough to prevent the circulation of rice, so that rice in the rural areas of the production area cannot be sold to the cities of the consumption area. To illustrate it with an example, the tax per dan of rice in Hunan is one yuan for passport fee, one yuan and two jiao for water freight, four jiao for sack, three jiao and two fen for export tariff, two jiao for rising and combining, two jiao for Hunan commission, two jiao for water insurance barge fee and customs declaration fee, two jiao for Shanghai fire insurance commission, totaling three yuan, three jiao and two fen. In Jiangxi, the passport fee is one yuan, the water freight is four qian per hundred jin, about eight jiao and five fen per bag, four jiao for sack, three jiao and three fen for export tariff, three jiao for rising and combining, two jiao for Jiangxi commission, two jiao for water insurance barge fee and customs declaration fee, two jiao for Shanghai commission fire insurance miscellaneous fees, totaling three yuan, one jiao and seven fen. In Wuhu, Anhui, the passport fee is four jiao, the water freight is three qian per hundred jin, about six jiao and five fen per bag, four jiao for sack, three jiao for export tax, five jiao for rising and combining, five liang per thousand taels for exchange water, three jiao for miscellaneous expenses, two jiao per shi for water insurance barge fee and customs declaration fee, totaling about three yuan (see page 33 of the first issue of China Economic). In other places, such as Sichuan, the land of abundance, the heavy taxes often cause the crops to rot in the fields. Therefore, as found in the Jiangsu investigation, the price of rice in the place of origin and in the city often differs by six or seven times (see the last chapter of Jiangsu Provincial Industrial Records). In this way, not only is it unprofitable for farmers to sell rice, but even at a loss, even rice dealers and rice merchants often stop. As reported by the Dagongbao on July 26 this year: [The food in Shanxi Province has always been surplus and sold to Hebei. Since the great harvest last year, not only has each county accumulated excess, forming a tragic phenomenon of low grain prices hurting farmers. Even in Taiyuan, this spring, grain merchants have suffered huge losses due to the slump in rice prices and sluggish sales. In addition, financial barriers and no way to sell goods have led to the successive closure of more than a dozen companies. However, in Hebei, from Shijiazhuang in the south to Shunde and Handan, and to Baoding in the north, according to a recent survey, the price of rice is almost equal to that of wheat. The lack of rice, beans and miscellaneous grains can be imagined. Shanxi and Hebei are close to each other, separated by a mountain, one side with overproduction; stockpiling and stagnation, and the other side with insufficient supply and high grain prices]. The reason for such stagnation is that, in addition to the high transport costs of the state-owned railways, which are disguised taxes, the direct blow is still the heavy taxes.

Second, another aspect of the food panic is the excessively low price of rice in the rice-producing areas, the so-called low grain prices hurting farmers: the reason is the same as the excessively high price of rice in the consumer market due to heavy taxes, which is still due to the excessive taxes. The heavy taxes make the price of rice too high on the one hand, and the price of rice falls on the other hand. This is not contradictory, but inevitable. Because farmers bear a heavy burden, they have to borrow money, or pre-sell grain, or sell the harvested rice urgently in order to pay taxes urgently. This will inevitably cause the price of rice to fall to the lowest limit, which is another aspect of the food panic.

The heavy taxes borne by farmers in various places are sometimes unbelievable. For example, in the He Tao regions, where [the Yellow River has a hundred diseases, only enriches one set], the heavy taxes borne by farmers have reached the point where the harvest from year-round hard work is not enough to pay taxes. Farmers have to flee, and the amount of wasteland is increasing day by day (22, 6, 15, Dagongbao). In the Zhenjiang and Huai'an areas of Jiangsu Province, the total amount of surtaxes exceeds ten times the regular tax. Every time something is started, there is one more surcharge. The affairs are replaced, but the surcharge always exists (22, 5, 28, Dagongbao). The burden on the farmers in Ningyuan makes even middle-class farmers unable to maintain it (22, 8, 2, ibid.). Jin County used to be a wealthy area, but in recent years, there have been many institutions and the burden has become heavier day by day. The peasant economy has been in a panic. The annual income, after all taxes and duties, is very little, and the people are in extreme distress (22, 7, 20, ibid.). The exorbitant taxes in Shaoyang are even more shocking. One tael of land tax requires the payment of more than fourteen yuan (22, 9, 6, ibid.). The heavy land taxes in Baoding caused poverty among farmers, to the extent that merchants dared not bid for contracts (22, 7, 11). In the northern counties of Jiangsu Province, [merchants are at a loss, and all businesses are becoming more and more declining. The counties of Huai, Lian, Si, Shu, Su and Sui add funding to the county-level institutions, all of which are taken from the farmers, who are exhausted to cope] (22, 10, 4, Da Wanbao). When tax collectors are hired, they have no choice but to sell the only food left to maintain their families at a low price. For example, last year [farmers in Shaanxi received one stone of grain, the market price was only three or four yuan, but from this one stone of grain, they had to pay taxes of eight or nine yuan. The tax exceeded the production price by one time. In order to pay the tax, farmers had to reduce their rice consumption and only eat porridge. The saved wheat and rice were moved to the cities for sale, so there was a lot of food on the market, with no way to go, and the price became even cheaper (21, 10, 16, Xi'an Daily). Some, in order to pay taxes, often pre-sell their rice before it is harvested (see Chapter 1, Chapter 3 of China's Rural Economic Data, Liming Bookstore). Even when the harvest comes, it is not enough to pay for the goods that have been pre-sold. Furthermore, in Sichuan Province, taxes are not fixed. As long as there is a war, there is an extortion. Today, the land tax has been pre-collected until 1996 (22, 7, 3, Shishi Xinbao). When faced with this kind of sudden extortion, farmers naturally have to sell their grain at [any price] to exchange for cash.

Third, another aspect of the food panic is that even if rice production is declining, one of the major reasons is closely related to taxation. The production cost of rice is much higher than that of soybeans and sweet potatoes. Taxation makes farmers generally poor, and as a result, they are unable to engage in rice production. According to the report of the Shanghai City Four Rural Areas Farm Cost Survey, the benefits of growing rice are much higher than those of growing soybeans. Most of the rice growers are owner-farmers, and most of the tenant farmers grow soybeans, and very few grow rice (Chapter 2 of China's Rural Economic Data). In various counties of Zhejiang Province, the planting area of sweet potatoes has reached the third place, and it is gradually expanding. There is no other reason for this, except that the cost of sweet potato planting is extremely low, from which we can know the relationship between the economic situation of farmers and the planting of agricultural products. Taxes make it impossible for farmers to maintain their livelihoods by growing rice and other food crops, and they have to switch to planting plants with higher profits, and opium is one of the main ones. For example, the "lazy tax" in Sichuan is simply forcing farmers to grow opium.

Fourth, the poverty of the farm economy caused by heavy taxation on the one hand leads to a reduction in rice production, and on the other hand leads to a reduction in consumption. It has become a common phenomenon for farmers not to eat rice. Not to mention the northern provinces, even in the central and southern provinces that mainly use rice as their staple food, the tendency of farmers' food to go from good to bad is also very obvious. For example, in Yuezhou, Hubei Province, grain is the main agricultural product, but very few farmers eat rice. The main food is sweet potatoes, beans, and sometimes a small amount of rice is mixed in for food (Hubei Goods and Medicine Magazine No. 104). Furthermore, as Marshall said; in most parts of Guangdong, sweet potatoes have accounted for the second place in farmers' food. In Zhejiang, most farmers have replaced rice with sweet potatoes (see Chinese Rural Economic Research). Since, due to the heavy taxes, it is not easy to transport rice from the place of origin to the consumer market, and at the same time, due to the poverty of the farm families, very few farmers in the rice-producing area eat rice, the rice will inevitably be stockpiled in the place of origin, forming another aspect of the food panic, [the surplus of food].

Therefore, whether directly or indirectly, the existence of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies is an obstacle to solving the food problem in China, which is beyond doubt. Without solving the tax problem, it is futile to tax foreign rice. However, today in China, whether it is the central government or the local government, even with the existing income from these taxes, they still feel financial difficulties. Therefore, how easy is it to abolish all the exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies that hinder the solution of the food problem?

Review of the Grain Storage System

— He Bing

Recently, the authorities telegraphed the governments of eight provinces, including Jiangxi and Hunan, to send representatives to discuss the food problem. The telegraph listed three fundamental policies for rescuing the rural areas. The second and third items are about the grain storage problem: "... (2) Handle grain storage and restore the old system of local granaries. Last year, the Wuchang Headquarters repeatedly ordered and sent letters to various provinces to urge the handling of this matter. You should check and handle it carefully and effectively. (3) It is proposed that the central government should use the cotton and wheat loan to create new warehouses in various provinces to handle active storage, loan borrowing, and transportation and sales in order to regulate the people's food, increase grain prices, circulate rural finance, and turn over funds in the future..." These two policies have the same effect, but different in nature. In my ignorance, I will briefly discuss what I know as follows:

First, all social phenomena have their own closely related aspects and a certain foundation, which varies with the times. The methods that are applicable in one era may not be applicable in another. It is impossible for the new dynasty to strive to restore the so-called "well-field" system before the Spring and Autumn Period. Regardless of how hard the restoration movement of the past dynasties tried, it was in vain. Today, the situation is the same when trying to restore the old-fashioned grain storage.

In the past, grain storage, such as social granaries and charitable granaries, was mainly based on farmers' voluntary storage of food. Its only foundation was built on the "local self-sufficient economy." At that time, the power of commodity exchange was not great. Not only was the agricultural production of a county relatively self-sufficient, but also most farmers could be self-sufficient. They used their own agricultural products for their own consumption. If there was a surplus, they could naturally store it to prevent famine. Whether it is a village, a clan, or a township, as long as it is in the same economic entity, a grain storage can be established.

But the current situation is completely different. Since the invasion of capitalism, the torrent of commodities has long broken the local self-sufficient economy based on families, villages, and even counties and provinces. As the local economy is destroyed, the grain storage system built on the local economy will naturally collapse.

According to all the current rural survey reports, it can be clearly seen that the farm economy in various parts of China has been completely commodified. Not only do they have to buy clothing and other supplies from the market, but also most of their food is bought from the market. On the other hand, for all kinds of needs, they mostly sell the harvested food after the autumn harvest, and rarely store it for their own use. They often sell their own food at a low price today, and buy back their own food at a high price tomorrow. This is not contradictory, because after the invasion of capitalism, nine out of ten farmers are in debt. In order to cope with high-interest loans, land rent, and taxes, they have no choice but to sell agricultural products at low prices in a hurry, but in hunger and cold, they have no choice but to endure the exploitation of commercial usurers, and endure the pain to borrow or buy some food to maintain their lives. In the past, farmers were self-sufficient in agricultural products and had a surplus, and they could establish grain storage to prevent famine. Now, farmers are groaning in the whirlpool of commodities, and they are helpless in hunger and cold. Under such a transformation, the grain storage system will inevitably be completely destroyed.

In addition to the farmers' voluntary storage, there were also local public granaries, mainly those of a clan or surname. But now, the "public fields" nominally public property in various places are monopolized by a few private individuals, and in recent years, the process of public fields joining the buying and selling has intensified, and most of them have successively fallen into the hands of private individuals. After the elimination of public property and public fields, the so-called public granaries based on public groups will naturally no longer be able to be rebuilt.

Therefore, the first type of old-fashioned grain storage is not only inevitably destroyed today, but also very difficult to restore.

Second, as far as the second type of new-style grain storage is concerned, as described in the telegram, its nature can be divided into two points. The first is to use the financial expenditure of the political storage to reward food and establish grain storage. The second point is to use this type of grain storage to operate food loans and regulate finance.

At first glance, no matter how the fundamental role of this type of new-style grain storage is, in terms of the nature of the first point, the government's finances have been exhausted in recent years, and it seems impossible to allocate some money from that part. If it is said that additional taxes are levied due to the handling of grain storage, it is harmful to the farmers before the benefits are seen, which is not what we hope. However, now it is said that a part is allocated from the cotton and wheat loan, and the situation seems to be different. The total amount of the cotton and wheat loan cannot be said to be small, but compared with the needs of various aspects of China today, it is really a drop in the bucket. Whether this matter can be realized, and whether the allocated part can be enough to carry out this small but huge work, can only be proved by future facts.

In terms of the second point, it is very common. The Jiangsu Farmers Bank and the Shanghai Xinhua Bank have carried out this kind of work in counties such as Wuxi and Wujin. But what is its effect?

"In the winter of 1920, the Farmers Bank operated rice loan borrowing in Lisha (Wuxi). The loan was 7 yuan per shi of white rice, with a monthly interest of 1%, an insurance fee of 1%, and a storage fee of 2%, a handling fee of 3%, totaling 1.6%. By the end of June of the following year, those who were unable to redeem it would sell the pledged rice to offset the principal and interest, and the surplus would be returned. Farmers and small landlords were forced to borrow money, and those who carried rice came in droves. The amount of loans reached more than 18,000 yuan. Last year, due to the flood and famine, the entire town's rice fields were submerged, and eight or nine out of ten people had no grain to harvest. However, the rice loan operated by the Farmers Bank and the Xinhua Bank was nearly 20,000 yuan; the rice collected by the landlords and the entire harvest of the farmers in Zoujin were almost entirely pledged." (Yu Linjun's survey, China's Rural Economic Data, page 413.)

This means that, in the case of the collapse of the entire rural economy that cannot be solved, this kind of institution is only like the pawnshops in various counties in Shaanxi and Jieyang, Guangdong today. There is a danger that there is a full loan but no one to redeem it, and they are forced to open the door. Therefore, the piecemeal construction of the grain storage problem cannot yet be called a fundamental relief policy.

The Central Question of the Tax on Foreign Rice: Is Taxing Beneficial to the Rural Areas?

— Liang Ming

According to the report on October 8; The Legislative Yuan's Finance Committee reviewed the import tax on foreign rice. Based on the national finance and the national economy, it decided to levy a tax. The highest tax rate is 2.50, and the lowest tax rate is tax-free. As for the detailed tax rate, the Ministry of Finance will formulate it by itself according to this established principle. Judging from this, the issue of taxing foreign rice, which has been delayed since the folk food conference last year and has been rumored frequently, is becoming more and more concrete, and the imposition of the tax seems to be not far away. Moreover, Guangdong, where the largest amount of foreign rice is imported, has already implemented it. Although rice merchants have repeatedly opposed it, the Guangdong government has firmly stated that it cannot withdraw its decision. There have also been many discussions on the issue of taxing foreign rice in recent months. The reason for taxing is nothing more than that the price of local rice has fallen, and taxing is to help farmers, which can also be said to be the first practical achievement shouted out in the past six months of "reviving the rural areas." However, in general discussions, the central question of whether taxing is beneficial to the rural areas is rarely fully explained.

First, we must first clarify the current situation of rice supply and demand: Anyone who knows a little about the general situation of China's rural economy knows that most of the farmers, who account for more than 80% of China's total population today, eat the lowest quality food such as corn, millet, sweet potatoes, pumpkins, and even wild vegetables. Used to fill the stomach. Except for landlords, rice-eating [rice] porridge and wheat rice is only a very small number of farmers. Therefore, the largest consumption of rice is in several large cities and a part of the towns. The composition of the population in cities is mainly industrial laborers and small white-collar workers. Rice does account for the most important part of their living expenses, so the price of rice is closely related to the livelihoods of these people. In previous labor strikes in Shanghai, a part of them were caused by the high price of rice, and laborers demanded an increase in "rice subsidies." Therefore, since the rice consumption market is mainly in large cities, and the rice-producing areas in China are not [limited] to each province, the transportation and regulation of rice has become the most important work. Of course, the competitive dumping of foreign rice is one of the reasons why local rice cannot stand. However, it cannot be denied that the collection of taxes in various provinces, the high transportation costs, and the obstacles such as the ban on exports often cause rice to be stockpiled in the place of origin, forming a surplus. Even within a province, sometimes between counties, they do not communicate with each other across borders. Other situations can be imagined.

Not only that, China currently implements a universal small-farmer system. The amount of rice produced by each farmer is limited and cannot directly reach the hands of consumers. It must be sold through intermediate merchants such as rice dealers and grain stores. The sale of rice by general farmers usually does not go beyond the following three forms: (1) Preselling at the time of showing harvest or even before sowing, (2) mortgaging due to borrowing money and saving food at the time of not harvesting and even not sowing, (3) immediately selling the harvested rice because they are anxious to pay rent and taxes as soon as the harvest is completed. When sold to rice dealers, grain stores or mortgaged to pawnshops through these three forms, farmers have absolutely no possibility of naturally choosing their selling price, and they can only let the other party decide. However, other methods are extremely rare in addition to these three forms of sale. We often read "Selling new silk in February, and new grain in May, treating the sore in front of us, but cutting out the flesh in our hearts." Unexpectedly, it is also a portrayal of modern rural areas.

Second, the result of taxing foreign rice is that imported foreign rice is consumed in cities. If the import tax on foreign rice is implemented, the price of rice will inevitably rise. After the news of the tax on foreign rice by the Guangdong Provincial Government spread, although it has not yet been implemented, the price of rice has risen, which can be used as proof. If the price of rice rises; if there are no supplementary measures, the price of rice will inevitably rise again. At this point, the industrial laborers who eat rice in the city and a part of the small white-collar workers will inevitably be greatly hit. Today, when the industrial recession is at its most severe, factories naturally have no power to increase the wages of workers and employees; what they can barely maintain is that the price of rice is cheap, and everything is also cheap. If the price of rice is high, not only will it not be able to stop the import of foreign rice, but the employees who rely on salary income will panic.

On the farmers' side, although not many farmers eat rice, the impact of the price increase on consumption is not as great as in the city, but it is not to say that no one eats rice. After the invasion of capitalism, the degree of commodification of agricultural products in China is very high. Many rice farmers do not eat the rice they produce themselves, but often sell the rice they produce themselves and buy rice on the market. This is a very common phenomenon in today's Chinese rural areas, which can be proved in various rural surveys. In this way, after the price of rice becomes expensive, the farmers who eat rice will also suffer a major blow. If it is said that the farmers who eat rice are mostly rich farmers and owner-farmers, the increase in the price of rice will promote the decline of rich farmers and owner-farmers, making the rural economy more and more likely to collapse.

The most important point of taxing foreign rice is to increase the price of local rice and increase the income of farmers. It is not to mention that not all farmers have recently planted rice. Even the farmers who plant rice will benefit less. After taxing foreign rice, the price of local rice may be increased, but this increase is mainly an increase in the price that rice merchants sell to consumers, not an increase in the price that producers sell to rice merchants. Because as long as the tenancy system, commercial usury, capital and exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies exist, farmers cannot but be poor. Because farmers are poor, they have to sell rice in one of the above three forms. In these three forms of sale, it is more of an exploitation than a sale. The benefit of the increased price of rice still does not go to the farmers. This is very important.

Therefore, in summary, taxing foreign rice, under the current situation, does not seem to have much effect on rescuing the rural areas. Moreover, if the Guangdong Provincial Government taxes foreign rice, it is said to be used to rescue the rural areas. However, according to the Guangzhou Correspondence in the Da Wanbao in September of this year, because the annual import of foreign rice in Guangdong Province is worth 60 to 70 million Hong Kong dollars, if 10% is taken from the value, the income can also reach between 8 and 9 million national currency. The current financial difficulty in Guangdong is only this, and a single move can solve the financial difficulty, so it should be done decisively. The intention of taxing can be seen.

General formalists believe that "yes" and "no" can be determined between the two extremes of facts. In reality, it is not that simple. If the dumping of foreign rice is not suppressed, Chinese local rice will never have a time to develop, and China's rural economy will only tend to collapse day by day. However, if the internal causes of rice production decline and food panic are not eradicated, and there is no unified method for production and sales, the role of taxing foreign rice is only to increase the burden of the people!

Commercial News

Financial: Foreign Exchange Loan Market Shrinks, Settlement Suspended

Yesterday was Sunday, and banks were closed as usual. The market was unusually bleak. Although native banks (錢莊) were open for business as usual, without the large-scale inflows and outflows of foreign banks, they were also much quieter. The market price of foreign exchange loans (洋拆) was consistently six fen in both the morning and afternoon sessions, a sharp drop of four fen compared to the previous day. The situation was quite loose and excessive. The volume of transactions in the loan market was over 4.3 million in the morning session, over 800,000 in new transactions, and over 200,000 in the afternoon session. Transactions at the Small Exchange Association totaled over 500,000. Native banks settled over 3.1 million in foreign promissory notes. There were no settlement records for foreign exchange forward contracts due to the bank holiday. As for the prices of subsidiary currencies, most were stable. The early morning price of Jiangsu small silver dollars (江南小洋) was 839 yuan, down five jiao (角) from the previous session. The price of Guangdong small silver dollars (廣東小洋) was 786 yuan, also down one yuan and five jiao from the previous afternoon session. In the afternoon session, Jiangsu small silver dollars fell another yuan to 838 yuan, while Guangdong small silver dollars rose one jiao to 786 yuan and one jiao. The trading volume for Jiangsu jiao was 8,000 jiao in the morning session and 5,000 jiao in the afternoon session. For Guangdong, the volume was 65,000 jiao in the morning session and 40,000 jiao in the afternoon session. Copper coins were released at a volume of 2,000 wen (文), totaling 303,000 wen, with transactions totaling 35,754 strings (串), equivalent to 11,800 yuan in silver.

Message Regarding the End of Semi-Annual Long-Term Loans

Yesterday, the 15th day of the 10th lunar month, was also the only period for the settlement of long-term loans. All long-term loan items made in the previous period (15th day of the 4th lunar month) with a six-month term were due yesterday and needed to be repaid or rolled over. It is understood that all merchant guilds (帮) have such long-term loans, with the Ningbo (甬) native banks issuing a significant amount. However, yesterday was a Sunday, a bank holiday. Therefore, Chinese banks that observe Sunday holidays could not process these transactions. Those that were open for half a day in the morning generally processed them. As a result, the total amount of these inflows and outflows for the day reached over 15 million. The situation can be categorized as follows: (1) Rollover of old account funds: over 3 million; (2) Matured loans extended because repayment was not possible: over 1.4 million; (3) Funds transferred to other banks: about 2 million; (4) Rollover of Ningbo native bank loans: over 4 million; (5) Newly issued loans: over 1 million; (6) Newly received term deposits: 2.8-2.9 million. In addition, there were new remittances from Ningbo native banks seeking lending opportunities in Shanghai, totaling over 1 million. A considerable amount of bank-related matters could not be processed due to time constraints and will need to be sorted out today. The interest rates set on that day varied widely, ranging from 7.5 to 11 taels, so a detailed breakdown cannot be provided.

Securities: Government Bonds Show Temporary Signs of Rising; Long and Short Positions Still Significant, Indicating Further Competition

During the past week, from October 9th to 14th, the market environment at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was stable. Although the issuance of new treasury bonds was substantial, they were not circulating in the market, and the financial sector saw a surplus of cash, which could be used as part of the reserve. With many short positions on the market, a short squeeze occurred on Monday, and market prices rose steadily. In particular, the supply of "Golden Long" bonds dried up, rising by 1.3 yuan. Other bonds also increased by 8-9 jiao to 1 yuan. Tuesday was the Double Tenth Festival, and the market was closed. When it reopened on Wednesday, the bulls showed some exhaustion and slight weakness. However, salt tax and "Golden Long" bonds continued to rise due to short covering, and subsequently continued to rise by 6-7 jiao. Most treasury bonds reached new highs. On Thursday, the 4th and 11th series were heavily traded, while the 50th series had weak absorption and fell by 6-7 jiao. On Friday, there was a lot of position switching between long and short parties, and market prices fluctuated. As a result, gains and losses were mixed. On Saturday, trading was extremely quiet, and the market was sluggish. As a result, declines outnumbered gains, and the range of highs and lows was only 1-2 jiao. Overall, the market price rose across the board during the week, ranging from 4-5 jiao to 1.2-3 yuan. The trend is temporarily fluctuating, but with significant long and short positions, further competition is expected. The total transaction volume for the week was 48,346,000 yuan, including 16,000 yuan in cash, 18,425,000 yuan in salt tax futures, 6,830,000 yuan in Jiji-Bing futures, 5,195,000 yuan in 1929 Customs bonds, 7,855,000 yuan in 1930 and 1931 Customs bonds, 5,725,000 yuan in the 1937 6% bonds, and other various bonds ranging from tens of thousands to over one million. 50 shares of stock were traded at the exchange.

American Cotton Affected by Increased Receipts

A telegram from New York dated the 13th reported on the cotton market for the week, stating that the cotton market was mixed and unstable. Although the government planned to release cotton loans and pay rental fees, the harvest estimates increased again. Prior to the government report, hedging sales and long liquidation hindered the rebound. However, the regulation of pledging one cent per pound is expected to be announced soon. The payment of rental fees, approximately between US$3 and US$11 per acre, will be allocated to cotton growers participating in next year's acreage reduction program, which aims to reduce cotton acreage to 25 million acres. This announcement will encourage cotton farmers to hoard their cotton and wait for the price of one cent per pound. If so, the spot position will inevitably tighten, and hedging sales will become sluggish. The Cotton Exchange estimates that world cotton consumption for August this year was 2,179,000 bales, compared to 1,819,000 bales at the same time last year. Therefore, this year's consumption is expected to be a constructive record.

Essays

On Fence-Sitting

—Wen Bing

Let me begin by citing a factual example, something similar to fence-sitting: the bat. There's a story about it: When the beasts of the land gathered, the bat went to participate. When asked about its qualifications, it said it could walk on the ground, like a rat. When the birds of the air gathered, the bat also went to participate. When asked about its qualifications, it said it could fly in the air, like a sparrow. In this way, the small bat can both walk and fly, just like an amphibious frog, at home in the water and equally at home on land. This expands its living space and naturally brings richer and more lasting enjoyment; its life seems more fulfilling and longer than usual.

Fence-sitting is just such a game. One foot on this side, the other on that, pleasing both. Here, I’m pointing out a human art of living, no, a unique life philosophy, because it’s similar to the bat, so it’s best to make a comparison.

Talking about fence-sitting is both verbose and hard to encompass; I have to make a summarized explanation. Where is its beauty? What’s it about? See below:

For example, your left and right neighbors are feuding enemies, locked in generations of resentment. It's hard to be in the middle. This is a good time to try fence-sitting. When your left neighbor tells you about your right neighbor's faults, you sympathize and nod. If he wants you to help set your right neighbor’s house on fire, aside from considering what will happen if the fire rises and you have to tear down your own eaves, you might as well lend a hand. Conversely, if your right neighbor tells you about your left neighbor's evil plot, you don't just sympathize and nod; it's best to stand up for justice and give a great speech about how base and poisonous your left neighbor is. If he plans to sue in court, your writing is sure to be sharp, so you might as well enthusiastically take on the task of drafting the complaint, just like Mao Sui recommending himself. But be careful; write it on the third shelf, sealing all the door and window gaps with paper, lest the news leak and your left neighbor loses face.

In this way, you will please both sides and gain mutual benefit: your east neighbor will invite you to drink and dine, and give you gifts for the New Year, and your right neighbor will make you the godfather of his son. To put it broadly, when you are in a difficult situation, borrowing grain or rice, or even borrowing thirty or fifty silver dollars, will be easy to obtain. In short, although your left and right neighbors are enemies, they treat you especially well; this is the best philosophy for everyday life.

For example, you can use the same technique in society. If you want to be active in politics and become an official, it's best to be good to Mr. X and also to Mr. Y, to the southwest and to the northwest. That way, the other side will naturally reciprocate, and it won't be difficult to have a smooth official career. Even if it is difficult to hold a high position in one place, you can always live privately, drawing a dry salary from one side and receiving a stipend from the other. When you go out, you can get travel expenses from here, and from there...

As for writers, they can also use fence-sitting. You have to be able to be new and old, radical and outdated. If a society is run by a certain faction, you propagate that faction's ideology; if another society requires a different approach, you switch tactics. If you're writing for a supplement or magazine, you have to be able to handle both old-style and new-style essays. If you cater to their taste, then your

Page 22

great work and name will shine in publications of the X faction, and you will also be able to establish a foothold in another XX faction.

That being said, sometimes things go wrong. After all, you are standing on two sides, and you put in a lot of effort. If your legs cramp, and your fence-sitting skills are maxed out, you might fall. But this is obviously an exception and a minority, so there's no need to worry so much.

In general, it requires a lot of top-notch self-cultivation; it's not something you can achieve in one jump. I’ve already said a lot. When I have time, I may write a sequel, "Fence-Sitting: Advanced Studies."

Major Events of the Week

—Shi Ben

The news that Chinese newspapers give us every day can be summed up in the four words "foul atmosphere and miasma." If you don't believe me, look at the facts.

4th, Nanjing dispatch: The Central Political Conference; the Ministry of Finance requested the issuance of 22 customs treasury bonds, worth 100 million yuan. The five principles and draft regulations were approved after discussion. 10th, Guangzhou dispatch: The Guangdong side is preparing to demand a shocking amount of money from Nanjing—190 million yuan—throwing out a political bomb.

3rd, Guangzhou dispatch: For several weeks, bomb attacks have occurred in various tea rooms in the city, totaling fifteen cases.

8th, Guangzhou dispatch: Chen Jitang is conducting a major search for dissidents, arresting over a hundred people in ten days, many of whom are university students. The Public Security Bureau has already executed nine.

5th, Beijing dispatch: Japanese troops in Miyun continue to increase in Huairou. The Huairou County Magistrate reported after fleeing to Tianjin: Over 700 Japanese troops in Miyun City are conducting demonstrations with live ammunition, bombing many civilian houses.

3rd, Nanjing dispatch: Prince De of Inner Mongolia is colluding with the Japanese and enticing independence, breaking away from the central government. The situation in all of Mongolia is becoming increasingly serious.

10th, Chongqing dispatch: Sichuan bandits have captured Sanhui. The bandit forces are rampant. Qu Guang and Shunpeng have declared martial law. The people are extremely panicked. Liu Xiang has set the bandit suppression military expenses at 4 million yuan and strictly ordered the county magistrates to be responsible for soliciting donations from wealthy gentry, to be paid in full by the end of October.

10th, Beijing dispatch: Japanese aircraft bombed Tangshan and other places. Two bombs each were dropped on Xiaotangshan, Hululu River, Daliushu, and Nieshan Camp. Houses were burned down. Residents suffered heavy losses and fled in droves.

10th, Beijing dispatch: The situation in Changli County is critical. Three thousand bandits are preparing to attack the city. The Japanese military police captain is collecting grain and fodder for the bandits. Yin Tong stated that the bandit suppression security team is still in its original location and has not yet moved east.

3rd, Tianjin dispatch: Traitors Xu Shoulin and Yang Zhixiang have illegally leased the Guangrentang cemetery to the Japanese Okura Trading Company to provide the Japanese army with land to build an airfield.

4th, Datong dispatch: Japanese people are entering Shanxi frequently. In ten days, seven or eight people have arrived in Shanxi. All are active-duty military officers, carrying cameras and acting suspiciously.

3rd, Beijing dispatch: A Japanese investigation team has penetrated into Mongolia for inspection, crossing the desert, heading to Xila Lianhe, crossing the Greater Khingan Mountains, and heading to Linxi.

3rd, Hangzhou dispatch: Jiangxi bandits attempt to peek into Zhejiang. The Director of Security, Yu Jishi, reported according to the report of Yang, the battalion commander of the 3rd battalion of the 3rd regiment that 500-600 Jiangxi bandits have occupied Xu village, which belongs to Kaihua County, and plan to attack Wangban.

8th, Kaifeng dispatch: Bandit forces are rampant in eastern Henan. Yang Xiaohei's gang has captured Dengcheng Village and kidnapped more than 600 people.

4th, Harbin dispatch: The Sino-Eastern Railway will... decisive action...

10th, Wuxi dispatch: A case of incest; coffin opened for verification.

Local news: Gongzu, Dingxin, and ten other factories are selling Japanese goods, falsely claiming they are Shenxin Clock brand national yarn and forging tax invoices.

Local news: On the Jisi Feier Road, robbers shot and killed the victim. Detectives waited and ambushed the robbers, and all four robbers were caught.

Qidong Dispatch (10th): The disaster situation in Qidong is serious. More than 100,000 disaster victims are crying from hunger and cold. It is unbearable to hear.

Local news: A dancing girl, XXX, accuses wealthy businessman Xu XX's son, Xu XX, of seduction and abandonment.

Local news: In the French Concession, two more major red pill manufacturing organizations were busted, seizing a large quantity of drug pills, white powder, and equipment.

3rd, Beijing dispatch: Fang Jibu fiercely attacked Datangshan and Xiaotangshan. Gaoli Camp was occupied. Intense fighting is taking place in Da Dongliu and Xiao Dongliu. Traffic between Ping and Tang has been cut off.

Alas! Look, is there any piece of news that is not filled with "foul atmosphere and miasma"? A few random selections are already filled with blood, tears, evil, poison, ugliness... Alas... Local news: Xu Leqing, a broker at the yarn and cloth exchange, was killed by bandits after they failed to kidnap him.

Local news: The first batch of American cotton has been completely sold off. The purchasers are all foreign merchants.

Local news: A teenage girl became pregnant after being raped in the third month of pregnancy; an abortion resulted in a tragic incident.

Local news: Disaster reports are pouring in from various places. Also, a love triangle resulted in a murder case.

Local news: Yue Qiao, the president of Kangjian Hospital, set a trap! How can there be any hope for such a society? Such a situation! How can people not lament!

Diplomas and Career Paths

— Donglin

A diploma is said to be a piece of paper that proves one's academic qualifications, eligibility, and level of education. Therefore, if you want to prove that you are a graduate of a certain university, specialized school, or middle school, you only need to drag out that precious "diploma" and show it off. It is also because of this reason that people spend a high price to "buy" or "forge" this precious item.

But in reality, how much of this is true? In fact, in today's society, those without diplomas are often well-fed, clothed, and carefree, but conversely, those with diplomas don't even have pants to wear.

According to a newspaper report a few days ago, a university graduate named Feng was arrested for forging a diploma to defraud money. Since Feng is a university graduate, he must have a diploma! But what use is the diploma to him?

On the streets of Shanghai, we can often see people spreading out their precious diplomas to beg for help. In short, this kind of "diploma incompetence" is not uncommon; Feng's case is just one example!

But, on the other hand, those people who enjoy all the happiness in life do not necessarily have diplomas! Some have never even seen that precious item in their entire lives!

Therefore, in today's distorted society, if you only have a diploma and want to find a career path, it is just a dream! But, if you don't have a diploma but have a special background and connections, then your career prospects are very promising. If you have both a special background, connections, and a diploma, that would be even better.

In summary, diplomas and career paths are not related. Without a certain intermediary, diplomas will never have any effect, and there will be no career path to speak of. That is to say, under special circumstances, there is a possibility of connection between diplomas and career paths. And, as long as this contradictory society exists, this phenomenon will continue.

Lunch

— Jiyun

A Shanghai person's breakfast. Except in the homes of the wealthy, where chefs cook elaborate snacks. Everyone else usually eats hastily. Congee, crab shell pastry, pan-fried buns, glutinous rice rolls, flatbread with fried dough sticks are the most common delicacies. The parasitic masters and mistresses in mansions listen to storytelling day and night and smoke opium. They don't go to bed until the sun is high. They only have white fungus, lotus seed soup, sweet osmanthus and white sugar porridge, lard and red bean paste eight treasure rice and other delicate things as late-night snacks. They fundamentally don't have breakfast. Many thrifty comrades drink a cup of plain water and a snack after washing in the morning. Anyway, lunch is not far away. They just tighten their belts.

As for dinner, the wealthy have banquets with each other. Dance halls, restaurants, clubs, and private restaurants come in all shapes and sizes and are too numerous to list. Ordinary people always eat a home-cooked meal at home.

Only lunch falls between morning and evening. It is most important for nutrition and the body. People who work during the day have the most variety of lunch styles. There are at least ten levels. However, their outcome is only to fill their stomachs. They all turn into rice excrement. They can also all extend life.

(1) Three-Day-Old Cold Rice - Saves a Penny

(2) Rickshaw Puller - Plain Noodles Plus Three - Fifteen Copper Coins

(3) Shop Clerk - Glutinous Rice Rolls, Fried Tofu, Vermicelli Soup - Twenty Copper Coins

(4) Junior Foreign Firm Employee - Buttered Bread or Beef Noodles - One Dime

(5) Mid-Level Foreign Firm Employee - Shen Wanxing or Wufangshou's Set Meal - Twenty-Two Cents

(6) Senior Employee - YMCA or Great China's Set Meal - Eighty Cents

(7) At Least a Foreigner - Deng Tuomo or Navy YMCA's Big Meal - One Dollar and Twenty Cents

(8) Small Manager - Shanghai and Citibank's Set Meal - Five Dollars

(9) Taipan - Licha and Huizhong Hotel's Set Meal - Ten Dollars

(10) The Wealthiest - Huate and other hotels' lavish meals - Fifteen to Fifty Dollars

Eaters ranging from "penniless" to dozens of gold can perhaps be jealous in sequence. But being able to "fill your stomach" is always the best. We think of those millions of compatriots who have been affected by disasters. Are their five senses, four limbs, and internal organs different from ours? They can't even find grass roots and tree bark. Being a "cold rice" comrade is not a blessing.

Drama

War and Peace (48) (A Play in Four Acts)

— He

Act Four: Where to Go? Scene One

What needs to be done is to collect... The common people are born to have their skin peeled and tendons drawn. When only a few bones are left, they will still come to suck our bone marrow! This is the relationship between the common people and the officials. But all my family members were killed by artillery fire, and my thatched hut was burned so that I can't find the direction. Only I am left as a bare stick in the ranks of the militia. I have guns in my hands, and if they dare to ask me for money, I can give them a bullet.

Soldier A: That's right, great! But there are many who don't have guns? What about them? Are they just waiting to die?

Soldier B: It's the same, those who don't want to die come to the militia!

Soldier C: (Rushing in from the left) Hurry, hurry, the Japanese soldiers are coming to clear the countryside.

Soldier Xin: How many people are there?

Soldier C: I don't know, I heard it's only a hundred or so guns. The village chief here invited them. They're about to enter the village.

Soldier A: Why should we leave? Is it the captain's order?

Soldier C: Of course, he said we have fewer people, they have more people, and we don't need to lose strength.

Soldier Xin: That makes a lot of sense. Let's disperse for now and wait for them to leave before we talk.

Soldier A: No, what are you talking about? We're not playing hide-and-seek with the Japanese soldiers, why should we hide? Where do we go to attack them?

Soldier B: Good, let's go to the village entrance on this side to ambush them. (Seeing the platoon leader coming from the left.) Platoon leader, we still have a machine gun, why should we run away? There is a small road at the village entrance on this side, with mountains on both sides. They must pass that way when they go back.

Soldier Wu: That's right, I also know that road clearly. There's no need to use guns at all. Just throw some big rocks down on both sides of the mountain, and you can kill them all cleanly.

Soldier C: But the captain's order is for us to retreat.

Platoon Leader: That's okay, the captain won't forbid us from fighting the Japanese soldiers. But do you all know that road?

Soldier Wu: I know, I'll take responsibility.

Platoon Leader: Good, it's your small team that will go. Are there any others?

Soldier Ding: They're in that forest, we have to pass that way.

(They take their weapons and exit from the right side of the stage.)

(The stage is temporarily silent, for about a minute, faint footsteps are heard. After a while, a youth comes up from the left in great tension and hides behind a big tree. After a while, a voice comes from afar.)

Voice: Big Monk... Big Monk...

Youth: Damn it, what are you shouting for!

Voice: ...Big Monk (Another youth comes up from the left.)

Youth: You're here, what's going on?

Youth: How is my family now?

Youth B: Your sister called Seventh Grandfather, he's pleading with Third Master Zhou.

Youth: Damn him, one day, I will chop him into minced meat.

Youth B: Tell me, what exactly is going on?

Youth: Seven or eight days ago, Third Master Zhou ran to my house to collect debts. Do you think anyone has money to pay debts at this time? I said "No." "No?" he said, "Is no enough to settle things?" I said, "What do you plan to do?" Later he said, "Okay, you wait, and see if you don't pay me back." Because of this, he hated me so much that he ran to the county town to accuse me, saying that I was a traitor. He said I was colluding with the Japanese army, colluding with some Li XX's troops, and fighting against the government. You think he is shameless!
